# Changelog

All notable changes to security-atlas are recorded here. Format follows
[Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/); versioning follows
[SemVer](https://semver.org/).

Release sections below are auto-generated by release-please from
Conventional-Commit messages. Each entry links to its slice issue, the
merging PR, and the squash-merge commit. For richer per-slice narrative
see the corresponding `docs/issues/<NNN>-*.md` and the PR body.

## Unreleased

### Changed

* **test: slice 411 — contract-tier goldens for the control-detail + audit-workspace routes.** Closes the slice-409 D1 / D6 deferral of the controls-detail (`/v1/controls/*`) and audit-workspace (`/v1/audit/*`) families. Lands the golden-file contract tier (ADR-0007) on the highest-traffic routes the `/e2e/` suite hand-mocks — the three control-detail tab reads (`web/e2e/control-detail-tabs.spec.ts` route-fulfills `/api/controls/{id}/{policies,risks,history}`) and the audit-workspace period index (`web/e2e/audits-header.spec.ts` reads `/api/audits` → `GET /v1/audit-periods`). **Seams (per-route, Option A):** an unexported `controlDetailReader` interface on the controldetail `Handler` carrying JUST the three read methods the policies/risks/history paths use (the `Evidence` tenant-wide-ledger path keeps the concrete `*Store` — deferred), and an unexported list-only `periodLister` on the auditperiods `Handler` carrying JUST `List`. Both are narrow by design (slice 409 D1 / slice 410 precedent: not a god-interface over the wider Store surfaces). `New(*Store)` / `New(*period.Store)` are byte-for-byte unchanged (P0-409-2): each wires the seam field to the same store, so production behavior is identical; every other handler keeps the concrete store. **Provider recorders** (`internal/api/controldetail/handler_contract_test.go` + `internal/api/auditperiods/handler_contract_test.go`, plus the shared `contractrecord_test.go` helper copied from slice 392/409/410) run on the plain `go test ./...` unit surface — no DB, no `//go:build integration` tag (P0-409-1) — injecting fixed-row stubs via the unexported `newHandlerWithReader` / `newHandlerWithLister`. The control-detail recorder routes through a chi mux so the `{id}` path param resolves (the difference from slice 410's query-param risks recorder). Four goldens (`web/lib/contracts/control-{policies,risks,history}.golden.json` + `audit-periods.golden.json`) record `populated` + `empty` variants exercising the nullable branches: opaque `inherent_score`/`residual_score` blobs + null `link_weight`, null `scope_cell`, and the omitempty `frozen_at`/`frozen_hash`/`frozen_by` (absent on open periods). **Verbatim-passthrough consumer asserts** (`web/lib/contracts/*.contract.test.ts`): unlike slice 410's transform-aware risks BFF, all four BFFs forward the upstream body unchanged (the lib fn returns `res.json()`; the route does `NextResponse.json(body)` / re-emits the upstream text), so the asserts are `toEqual(golden)` like the slice-409 dashboard panels. **Drift proven:** renaming `link_weight` → `weight` in `control-risks.golden.json` failed both halves (provider wire-shape mismatch; consumer `link_weight: expected false to be true`); golden restored, both green. **Zero-new-gate** (AC-4): rides the existing Go-unit + vitest surfaces; auditperiods gained a first unit-surface suite (0% → 14%), controldetail's merged 90% floor is unaffected (the seam is integration-covered + the recorder adds unit coverage). **Deferred (spillover):** the controls-detail long tail (`coverage`/`effectiveness`/`state`/`attestations` — separate packages `ucfcoverage`/`controlstate`/attest) and the audit-workspace tail (`populations`/`samples`/`walkthroughs`/`notes`) → slice 412. **Type: JUDGMENT** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/411-contract-tier-controls-audit-decisions.md`. Slice doc: `docs/issues/411-contract-tier-controls-audit-routes.md`. Parent: slice 409.
* **test: slice 410 — contract-tier golden for the dashboard top-risks panel (`GET /v1/risks`).** Closes the slice-409 D1 deferral of the dashboard top-risks panel. Adds the golden-file contract tier (ADR-0007) to `GET /v1/risks` so the slice-210 class of silent BFF↔atlas wire-shape drift is caught at the cheapest surface (Go-unit + vitest). **Seam (list-only Option A):** an unexported `riskLister` interface on the risks `Handler` carrying JUST the `List` method the `ListRisks` path uses — deliberately narrow rather than a ~7-method interface over the wide `*risk.Store` surface (Create/List/Get/Delete/Heatmap/ThemeOrgUnitHeatmap/…) a single golden would not justify (slice 409 D1). `New(*risk.Store)` is byte-for-byte unchanged (P0-409-2): it wires `lister` to the same store, so production behavior is identical; every other handler keeps the concrete `*risk.Store`. **Provider recorder** (`internal/api/risks/handler_contract_test.go`, plus the shared `contractrecord_test.go` helper copied from slice 392/409) runs on the plain `go test ./...` unit surface — no DB, no `//go:build integration` tag (P0-409-1) — injecting a fixed-row stub via the unexported `newHandlerWithLister`. The golden (`web/lib/contracts/risks.golden.json`) records `populated` + `empty` variants of the upstream `{risks: riskWire[], count}` envelope, including the opaque `inherent_score`/`residual_score` JSON blobs, the `linked_control_ids` array (populated + empty), and the nullable `review_due_at`/`accepted_until` (present on one row, omitted on another). **Transform-aware consumer assert** (`web/lib/contracts/risks.contract.test.ts`): unlike the slice-409 passthrough panels, the dashboard/risks BFF unwraps `body.risks` and re-wraps `{risks, count: risks.length}`, so the assert checks the BFF output equals `{risks: golden.risks, count: golden.risks.length}` — NOT `toEqual(golden)`. **Drift proven:** renaming `treatment` → `treatment_kind` in the golden failed both halves (provider wire-shape mismatch; consumer `treatment: expected 'undefined' to be 'string'`); golden restored, both green. **Zero-new-gate** (AC-4): rides the existing Go-unit + vitest surfaces; risks-package unit coverage rose 4.5% → 13.8%. **Type: JUDGMENT** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/410-contract-tier-risks-panel-decisions.md`. Slice doc: `docs/issues/410-contract-tier-risks-panel.md`. Parent: slice 409.
* **ci: slice 408 — integration-enrolment drain batch 8 (catalog/oscal/policy/risk tail) — closes slice 390.** Eighth and **final** batch of the slice-390 enrolment-backlog drain (sequential after slice 407); merging it shrinks `KNOWN_UNENROLLED` from 5 to **0** and closes slice 390. Five packages carried a `//go:build integration` tag but were absent from the `tests-integration` job's package list (catalogued by the slice-345 enrolment guard), so their integration suites had **never run in CI**: `internal/catalog/metrics`, `internal/oscal`, `internal/policy/pdf`, `internal/policy/seed`, `internal/risk/aggrule`. Added all five (per-leaf recursive `./internal/<pkg>/...`, each a single leaf package with one `integration_test.go` plus production source and no tracked subpackages — the bare-root form from slices 403/406 does not apply) to the `go test -tags=integration` invocation, inserted before the bare `./internal/api` root, and **emptied the slice-345 `KNOWN_UNENROLLED` allowlist** (monotonic shrink 5→0; the array is now intentionally empty; the guard self-handles the empty case — self-test 12/12 green; audit reports 87 tagged / 87 enrolled / 0 waived). **No test broke** — all five suites passed unmodified, in isolation and in a forced-uncached combined serial `-p 1` run (both orderings) alongside the contaminating `internal/demoseed` neighbour; no FK-wipe contamination surfaced. `internal/oscal`'s `TestExport_FrozenPeriodProducesSignedBundle` self-skips when the optional Python compliance-trestle bridge subprocess is unavailable (decision D2 in the test file) — this is pre-existing documented optional-precondition behaviour, identical local and in CI (CI provisions no Python bridge), NOT a masked failure; the load-bearing Aggregate-side invariant-10 "refuse a non-frozen period" check runs with no bridge. The slice-386 `metrics_catalog` NULL-encoding fix (`nonNilStrings` empty-slice→`[]` not SQL NULL on the NOT-NULL `source_slices` column) is genuinely exercised — `seed_test.go` asserts `nonNilStrings(nil)`/`nonNilStrings([])` both return non-nil and the integration `SeedFromEmbedded` round-trips the real INSERT. **Coverage:** four packages already carried hard floors honest against own-suite measurements (`catalog/metrics 76` vs 94.2%, `oscal 69` vs 78.9%, `policy/seed 87` vs 89.5%, `risk/aggrule 72` vs 74.6%) — left unchanged (conservative ratchets). `internal/policy/pdf` lifted off `excludes` to a new floor `68` (`floor(70.8 − 2)`). **Latent exclude-shadow bug fixed in-place:** the `internal/policy/` excludes prefix (intended only for the root `internal/policy` handler package) silently shadowed *every* `internal/policy/*` subpackage in `cmd/scripts/coverage-gate` (a package matching any exclude prefix is skipped), so the pre-existing `internal/policy/seed: 87` floor was dead config and the new `policy/pdf: 68` floor would have been too. Removed the blanket `internal/policy/` exclude (+ its `$exclude_justifications` entry) and gave the root its own honest floor `internal/policy: 35` (`floor(37.1 − 2)`), un-shadowing the seed/pdf subpackage floors so they are now actually enforced (verified via merged-profile gate run: all policy-family floors checked + passing, none skipped). **Final slice-390 tally** across all eight batches: real finds were slice 314 (device-flow `postForm` 404), slice 402 (a real `adminauditlog` product bug + a stale tenancy-middleware test), slice 405 (`ucfcoverage` stale-test + a genuine `TRUNCATE … CASCADE` FK-wipe contamination fix), slice 406 (stale OIDC nonce-ordering test); the benign batches were 401/403/404/407 and this one (no test broke). `KNOWN_UNENROLLED` is now **empty** — the slice-345 ratchet has reached zero and the structural enrolment gap slice 390 set out to close is closed. **Type: AFK** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/408-integration-drain-batch-8-decisions.md`. Slice doc: `docs/issues/408-integration-drain-batch-8-catalog-oscal-policy-risk-tail.md`. Parent: slice 390.

None of the four has unit tests (0.0% unit), so the merged profile equals the integration-only number; floors are conservative own-suite-anchored bounds. **Type: AFK** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/407-integration-drain-batch-7-decisions.md`. Slice doc: `docs/issues/407-integration-drain-batch-7-freshness-drift-family.md`. Parent: slice 390.
* **ci: slice 406 — integration-enrolment drain batch 6 (auth substrate + keystore).** Sixth batch of the slice-390 enrolment-backlog drain (sequential after slice 405). Four packages carried a `//go:build integration` tag but were absent from the `tests-integration` job's package list (catalogued by the slice-345 enrolment guard), so their integration suites had **never run in CI**: `internal/auth`, `internal/auth/keystore/fsstore`, `internal/mcp`, `internal/observability/otel`. Added all four to the `go test -tags=integration` invocation — `internal/auth` enrolled as the **bare root** `./internal/auth` (it holds a single `package auth_test` `integration_test.go` exercising the slice-034 users/sessions/api_keys RLS round-trips; the `./internal/auth/...` recursive form would double-enrol the oidc/jwtmw/users/oauth* subpackages that are tracked and enrolled separately, mirroring the slice-403 api-root bare-form precedent and the existing `./internal/audit` bare entry), and the other three per-leaf recursive — inserted before the bare `./internal/api` root, and removed all four from the slice-345 `KNOWN_UNENROLLED` allowlist (monotonic shrink 13→9; guard self-test 12/12 green; audit reports 78 enrolled / 9 waived). **One silently-broken test surfaced** (the never-run failure class, matching slices 314/402/405): `internal/auth`'s `TestOIDC_CallbackStateMismatchRejected` failed with `ErrNonceMismatch` instead of the expected `ErrStateMismatch`. **Stale-test fix, not a product bug**: slice 365 added an OIDC ID-token-replay guard that checks the `NonceCookie` *presence* before the state-mismatch (CSRF) check in `HandleCallback`. The pre-365 test set State/Verifier/Idp cookies but never set the new NonceCookie, so the flow short-circuited at the nonce-presence gate before reaching the state check it is named for. The ordering is correct, intentional, and locked by slice 365's P0-365-1; the fix is to set a non-empty NonceCookie so the test exercises the state-mismatch path (mirroring the canonical slice-365 `ErrStateMismatch` test in `oidc_nonce_integration_test.go`). No test skipped or deleted. The sibling `TestOIDC_CallbackMissingCookieRejected` (no cookies at all) still correctly returns `ErrStateMismatch` at the first cookie check. **No FK-wipe contamination**: the auth suite scopes every test to a fresh random tenant UUID and cleans up via the admin (`BYPASSRLS`) pool, and `mcp`/`otel`/`fsstore` do not touch the shared DB (fake HTTP platform / in-memory exporter / `t.TempDir()` keystore respectively); a combined serial `-p 1` run alongside the contaminating `internal/demoseed` neighbour stayed green. **Coverage**: no floor changes — `internal/auth/keystore/fsstore` (74), `internal/mcp` (80), `internal/observability/otel` (92) already carry hard floors enforced against the slice-279 merged unit+integration `-coverpkg=./...` profile, and enrolment of their own integration suites can only raise the merged number; `internal/auth` (the bare path) holds **no `package auth` production code** (only the external `auth_test` integration suite), so `go test -cover` reports `[no statements]` — it needs neither a floor nor an `excludes` entry (honest per slices 396/401–405, cleaner than the `emptyset` doc.go case). **Type: AFK** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/406-integration-drain-batch-6-decisions.md`. Slice doc: `docs/issues/406-integration-drain-batch-6-auth-substrate-+-keystore.md`. Parent: slice 390.
* **ci: slice 405 — integration-enrolment drain batch 5 (api domain handlers B).** Fifth batch of the slice-390 enrolment-backlog drain (sequential after slice 404). Five packages carried a `//go:build integration` tag but were absent from the `tests-integration` job's package list (catalogued by the slice-345 enrolment guard), so their integration suites had **never run in CI**: `internal/api/questionnaires`, `internal/api/ucfcoverage`, `internal/api/emptyset`, `internal/api/freshnessdrift`, `internal/audit/notes`. Added all five (per-leaf recursive) to the `go test -tags=integration` invocation, inserted before the bare `./internal/api` root, and removed them from the slice-345 `KNOWN_UNENROLLED` allowlist (monotonic shrink 18→13; guard self-test 12/12 green; audit reports 74 enrolled / 13 waived). **One silently-broken test surfaced** (the never-run failure class, matching slices 314/402): `internal/api/ucfcoverage`'s `TestControlCoverage_Slice256_InScopeRowReturnsNumeric` failed because its setup never seeded a `scope_cells` row — the control's legacy match-all `applicability_expr` resolved against an empty scope-cell universe, so the row rendered out-of-scope and coverage came back `null`. **Stale-test fix, not a product bug** (the null is the documented correct behaviour for an empty universe): added a `seedScopeCell` helper, seeded one cell in the in-scope test, and added `scope_cells` to `wipeTenantState`'s cleanup so it does not leak across tests. No test skipped or deleted. **A second `ucfcoverage` bug then surfaced in CI** — a genuine test-isolation FK-wipe bug (the whole suite failed with RESTRICT-FK violations, SQLSTATE 23503). Both wipe helpers did a global `DELETE FROM controls` without clearing the FK dependents, and under CI's serial `-p 1` run prior packages (`internal/demoseed` + the audit-sample suites) leave rows referencing controls under the shared tenant. The FK closure is deep — `sample_evidence → evidence_records → controls`, all `ON DELETE RESTRICT` — so enumerating children is whack-a-mole (an enumerate-children first attempt just advanced the error one level deeper to `sample_evidence_evidence_fk`). Fixed robustly with `TRUNCATE … CASCADE` (`TRUNCATE controls RESTART IDENTITY CASCADE`, and `TRUNCATE controls, framework_scopes, scope_cells RESTART IDENTITY CASCADE`), which clears the full transitive dependent set atomically and does not touch `scf_anchors`/`tenants` — mirroring the repo's existing TRUNCATE-CASCADE precedent (`internal/evidence/ingest`, `internal/platform/status`). Test-harness-only fix (no product change, `ucfcoverage` floor unchanged at 70). Reproduced the exact deeper CI condition locally (full `sample_evidence → evidence_records → controls` contamination chain under the shared tenant) and verified the fix resolves it in the faithful `demoseed → ucfcoverage` `-p 1` ordering, clearing the contaminating `sample_evidence`/`evidence_records` rows. **Coverage floors** added at `floor(own_suite − 2)`: `questionnaires 54` (56.6%), `ucfcoverage 70` (72.2%), `freshnessdrift 81` (83.6%), `audit/notes 83` (85.0%); `ucfcoverage`/`freshnessdrift`/`audit/notes` lifted off `excludes` (+ their `$exclude_justifications` entries removed), `questionnaires` was never gated and gains its first hard floor. `internal/api/emptyset` is a **zero-statement package** (`doc.go` only; the cross-cutting empty-set sweep lives in an external `_test` package) — it reports `[no statements]`, so it is **kept on `excludes`** rather than given a fabricated floor (honest per slices 396/401–404). Transitive coverage from the existing CI list is small in every case (≤5.6% vs own-suite 56.6–85.0%), confirming the own-suite-anchored floors are real, conservative ratchets, not transitive-load phantoms. **Type: AFK** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/405-integration-drain-batch-5-decisions.md`. Slice doc: `docs/issues/405-integration-drain-batch-5-api-domain-handlers-B.md`. Parent: slice 390.

* **test(e2e): slice 399 — fix bff-cookie prod-build spec + make prod-build CI leg blocking (closes slice 387 spillover).** Slice 387 built the `frontend-playwright-prod-build` CI harness (build:standalone → boot `node .next/standalone/web/server.js` → `ATLAS_PROD_BUILD=1`) and shipped it ADVISORY/logo-only because the companion `web/e2e/bff-cookie-production-build.spec.ts` (slice 146) carried two dev-server-shaped assumptions that had never executed until the harness existed. If the slice-146 fix is reverted the standalone server drops the cookie, the RSC render fails auth → login page → "Sign out" disappears and/or any client panel fetch surfaces "Unexpected token '<'" — the spec fails red on the regression it guards. **(AC-2) Assertion 2 cookie-domain fix.** `context.addCookies` now derives the cookie domain from the Playwright `baseURL` (the served origin) instead of `new URL(authedPage.url())` — before navigation `authedPage.url()` is `about:blank`, whose empty hostname made Playwright reject the cookie ("Cookie should have a url or a domain/path pair"). Same baseURL-origin pattern `web/e2e/fixtures.ts` already uses for the bearer cookie. **(AC-3)** `.github/workflows/ci.yml`'s `frontend-playwright-prod-build` job now runs BOTH prod-build specs (`bff-cookie-production-build.spec.ts` + `logo-render-production-build.spec.ts`) and `continue-on-error: true` is removed — the leg is now blocking. **(AC-4)** the slice-153 logo spec is unchanged and still runs. Uses `ATLAS_JWT_COOKIE` (renamed in slice 397). Deterministic: Playwright auto-waiting web-first assertions + the `response` event listener, no fixed sleeps. The `test.skip(!ATLAS_PROD_BUILD)` guard is retained (scopes the spec to the standalone leg, prevents dev-server green-washing). `.github/branch-protection.json` NOT modified (promotion to a required check is a follow-up after green runs, per slice 387 D6). **Type: JUDGMENT** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/399-bff-cookie-prod-build-spec-fix-decisions.md`. * **refactor(web): slice 397 — rename `SESSION_COOKIE` → `ATLAS_JWT_COOKIE` (closes slice 328 M-3).** The BFF cookie constant exported from `web/lib/auth.ts` was named `SESSION_COOKIE` but, since slice 206, resolves to the JWT cookie value `"atlas_jwt"` — a misleading name flagged by the slice 328 code-review audit as finding M-3 ("the underlying behavior is correct, only the symbol name is misleading"). Slice 328 §D4 recommended bundling the rename into slice 370; slice 370 D2 deferred to slice 395 (Phase 2 import migration); slice 395's hard no-touch rule on `web/lib/contracts/` (slice 349/392 golden tier) forced an atomic symbol rename — which must touch the two golden-tier contract *tests* that import the symbol — to split out here. **Pure symbol rename, zero wire/value change (P0-397-1):** the cookie value stays `"atlas_jwt"`; every `cookies().get/set/delete` and BFF `Authorization: Bearer` forward is byte-identical in behavior — only the identifier changed. **354 bare `SESSION_COOKIE` occurrences renamed across 127 files** (BFF routes, `web/proxy.ts` middleware, `web/lib/api/bff.ts`, `web/app/login/actions.ts` cookie writer, components, e2e + e2e-audit fixtures/specs, `web/scripts/capture-readme-screenshots.ts`'s standalone local const, and the two golden-tier contract tests `me.contract.test.ts` + `demo-status.contract.test.ts`) via a word-boundary-aware `perl -i 's/\bSESSION_COOKIE\b/ATLAS_JWT_COOKIE/g'` codemod. **`OIDC_SESSION_COOKIE` is a distinct cookie (`"atlas_session"`) and was NOT touched (P0-397-2):** the `\b` word boundary provably does not match the `SESSION_COOKIE` substring inside `OIDC_SESSION_COOKIE` (the preceding `_` is a word char), verified to remain at all 38 occurrences. The self-acknowledging rename-intent comment at `web/lib/auth.ts:10-14` was rewritten to reflect the completed rename. **No golden shape changed:** only the two `*.contract.test.ts` harness files' local `cookieStore.set(...)` identifier moved; no `*.golden.json` recorded contract was touched (JUDGMENT note in the slice doc confirms this narrow golden-tier-test touch is the mechanical-local-edit kind, not a contract-semantics change). **AC-1:** `web/lib/auth.ts` exports `ATLAS_JWT_COOKIE`, no `SESSION_COOKIE` export remains, `OIDC_SESSION_COOKIE` unchanged. **AC-2:** zero bare `SESSION_COOKIE` references remain (grep-clean, excluding `OIDC_SESSION_COOKIE`). **AC-3:** `tsc --noEmit`, `npm run lint` (0 errors; 2 pre-existing unused-eslint-disable warnings in the screenshots script, unchanged from `main`), all 1204 vitest tests across 122 files (incl. golden-tier contracts), and a full `next build` all green; the Playwright e2e suite (requires the full atlas + Postgres + `/v1/test/issue-jwt` stack) runs in CI — the rename is compile-time-only and the e2e specs typecheck + the production build compiles every module they import. **No auth/cookie bug surfaced** — the three load-bearing auth files (`bff.ts`, `proxy.ts`, `login/actions.ts`) show identifier-only diffs. **Does NOT auto-merge — golden-tier touch needs review (P0-397-3).** **Type: JUDGMENT** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/397-session-cookie-symbol-rename-decisions.md`. * **test(e2e): slice 388 — board-pack export end-to-end (closes slice 351 spillover).** Adds `web/e2e/board-pack-export-e2e.spec.ts`, the missing half of flow #12 in slice 351's e2e critical-flow coverage matrix (`docs/audits/351-e2e-critical-flow-coverage-matrix.md`): the existing `board-pack-detail.spec.ts` only exercises the UI render of a board pack, never the generate → render → download-PDF chain. Board-pack export is a v1 binary success-test flow (CLAUDE.md: "generate the next board pack from it"), flagged half-covered by both slice 333 Q-9 and the slice 351 matrix (P1, deferred there per anti-criterion P0-1). The spec models the full export chain: (1) **generate** — an in-page `fetch` POST `/api/board-packs` returns a DRAFT `BoardPack` carrying a known id (the `evidence-push-e2e.spec.ts` precedent: `page.request` is not page-route-intercepted, so the POST is driven via `page.evaluate` to flow through the page network); (2) **render** — navigate `/board-packs/{id}`, gated on the `getBoardPack` detail GET round-trip (slice 275 `waitForResponse`-before-`goto` pattern), assert the sticky `ExportBar` and its `export-pdf-link` anchor pointing at the slice-043 BFF passthrough `/api/board-packs/{id}/pdf`; (3) **download** — click the link and assert a `download` event fires with a `.pdf` suggested filename and `%PDF`-prefixed bytes. Two notable e2e mechanics, both documented inline: the PDF link carries `target="_blank"`, so the download surfaces on a popup context (`context.waitForEvent("download")`, not `page`), and every `route.fulfill` mock registers on the browser **context** rather than the page so the popup's PDF request is intercepted too. Follows the established `route.fulfill` mock convention (slice 351 P0-4) — the chromedp-backed PDF-bytes render (slices 340/341) is server-side and already pinned by the chromedp specs, so per the slice doc the spec is scoped to the BFF generate + download-trigger boundary. Mocked-payload schema-conformance follows the slice 276 lesson (the DRAFT pack satisfies the producer-side `BoardPack` type, with a section for every `BOARD_PACK_SECTION_KEYS` entry). Deterministic (AC-3): no sleeps, auto-waiting assertions, `waitForResponse`/`waitForEvent` gates; validated locally 3/3 under `--repeat-each=3` (3 parallel workers, confirming `fullyParallel` safety). ADDITIVE — does not re-implement `board-pack-detail.spec.ts`, and does not touch the board-narrative AI-assist surface (constitutional; out of scope). **Type: AFK.** Slice doc: `docs/issues/388-e2e-board-pack-export-end-to-end.md`.

* **test(e2e): slice 389 — multi-tenant JWT harness + real-RLS cross-tenant-leak spec (closes slice 351 spillover).** Extends the env-gated test-only `POST /v1/test/issue-jwt` endpoint (`internal/api/testissuejwt.go`) to mint a genuine MULTI-tenant JWT: two new OPTIONAL request fields — `available_tenants[]` and `roles_by_tenant` — let the e2e harness mint a JWT whose `atlas:available_tenants[]` spans 2 tenants (the shape the RFC 8693 token-exchange tenant-switch requires). When `available_tenants` is omitted the minted JWT is single-tenant, byte-identical to the slice-201 shape (strictly backward compatible). The extension does NOT widen the production attack surface (P0-201-4): the endpoint is still gated by `ATLAS_TEST_MODE` at both mount time (`httpserver.go`) and request time, still signs through the single `s.jwtSigner` (no parallel test-only signer), and adds a NEW constraint — `tenant_id` MUST be a member of `available_tenants` (rejected 400 otherwise), mirroring `jwt.Validate`'s tenant-scope invariant; malformed UUIDs in the set are also 400. New Go unit tests cover the multi-tenant mint, single-tenant backward compat, the current-tenant-not-in-available 400 guard, and the malformed-UUID 400. Adds the real-Postgres-RLS spec `web/e2e/tenant-switch-rls.spec.ts` (the depth assertion slice 351's mocked `tenant-switch.spec.ts` deferred here, per slice 333 Q-9): it seeds a known "canary" risk in tenant A only (`fixtures/e2e/tenant-switch.sql` + new `seed.ts` fixture name), authenticates a multi-tenant user, asserts the canary IS visible while current_tenant = A, switches to tenant B via the REAL token-exchange (BFF → `/oauth/token`), and asserts the canary is NOT visible in the tenant-B view through genuine PostgreSQL Row-Level Security — constitutional invariant #6, the v1 binary tenant-isolation criterion, asserted through the real stack rather than a `route.fulfill` mock. The slice-351 mocked spec is unchanged (stays the fast flow-level gate). **Load-bearing judgment (decisions log D4):** the spec mints with `super_admin: true` because super_admin is an OPA-authz + token-exchange-allowlist concept ONLY — it does NOT bypass PostgreSQL RLS (jwtmw sets `app.current_tenant` from the verified claim regardless, P0-190-3), so the cross-tenant-leak assertion is exactly as strong while giving the synthetic (no `user_roles`) test user a clean authz read path; a super_admin=false synthetic JWT would 403 at OPA before RLS ran, masking the test. **Type: JUDGMENT** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/389-multi-tenant-jwt-rls-leak-spec-decisions.md` (D1 optional-fields over a second endpoint; D2 production-safety review; D3 risks-not-controls assertion target; D4 super_admin-vs-RLS reasoning; D5 tenants identity-row seed; D6 responsive duplicate-title disambiguation; D7 does-not-replace-351). Slice doc: `docs/issues/389-e2e-multi-tenant-jwt-real-rls-leak-spec.md`.

* **refactor(api): slice 369 — consolidate `writeJSON`/`writeError`/`writeServerErr` into `internal/api/httpresp` (closes slice 328 H-1).** Slice 328's code-review audit (finding H-1) surfaced 103 byte-identical response-helper declarations across 50+ `internal/api/*` packages: 40 `writeJSON`, 45 `writeError`, 18 `writeServerErr` (the slice doc's "101" headline under-counted the two `status`-rename `writeJSON` variants — decisions log D6). New package `internal/api/httpresp` (mirror of slice 367's `internal/api/httperr`) exports `WriteJSON(w, status, body)` and `WriteError(w, status, msg)`; the two packages partition the response surface with zero overlap — `httpresp` owns 2xx + 4xx (success bodies, user-input errors), `httperr` owns 5xx (generic body + `request_id` + slog, CWE-209). 1131 call sites (`writeJSON` 240, `writeError` 771, `writeServerErr` 120) rewritten via `gofmt -r` AST-exact rewrites; all 103 declarations deleted. The 18 `writeServerErr` adapters were all trivial `httperr.WriteInternal` delegates (none doing sentinel-mapping work per P0-369-3) and now call `httperr.WriteInternal` directly, closing slice 367 §D2's deferred follow-up. Parameter standardised on `status int` (net/http convention) over the legacy `code int` majority (D1). **Pure refactor — no wire change (P0-369-1):** the new `internal/api/httpresp/httpresp_test.go` pins the exact byte stream (trailing `json.Encoder` newline, `{"error": msg}` envelope, JSON escaping) at 100% statement coverage; the bodies were verified byte-identical before migration. **Regression guard:** new `cmd/scripts/duphelper-lint` analyzer (mirror of slice 367's `errleak-lint`: `golang.org/x/tools/go/analysis` + `analysistest` fixture) rejects any new package-local `writeJSON`/`writeError`/`writeServerErr` free-function declaration in `internal/api/*` (methods and the exported shared names are not flagged); wired into the `justfile` `lint` target as `lint-duphelper`. **AC-5 contract locks:** `internal/api/metrics/handlers_test.go`'s two response-shape tests now assert `httpresp.WriteJSON`/`WriteError` directly, and `internal/api/board/integration_test.go`'s 400-path test gains explicit `application/json` + `{"error": ...}` envelope assertions. `internal/api/policyacks`'s now-orphaned local `errorBody` struct removed (D7); `internal/api/evidence`'s `errorBody` kept (still used for richer 4xx envelopes via direct `httpresp.WriteJSON`). No coverage floor regresses — removing covered trivial statements never lowers a package's percentage (D9), so the slice-069 ratchet is untouched. **AC-4 partial in this PR:** the analyzer's CI hard-failure step is deferred to spillover slice 391 (`docs/issues/391-duphelper-lint-ci-wiring.md`) because batch-164 reserved `.github/workflows/ci.yml` for slice 345 this batch; the local `just lint` guard enforces it today. **Type: JUDGMENT** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/369-httpresp-shared-helper-consolidation-decisions.md` (D1 `status int`; D2 httpresp/httperr clean partition + static-500-message edge case; D3 retire-all-18 writeServerErr; D4 analyzer reject-all-from-day-one; D5 CI wiring deferred to slice 391; D6 count reconciliation; D7 errorBody disposition; D8 AC-5 test rewiring; D9 coverage). Slice doc: `docs/issues/369-httpresp-shared-helper-consolidation.md`.

* **ci: slice 345 — integration-job enrolment-discovery guard (closes slice 334 I-1).** Adds `scripts/audit-integration-enrolment.sh` plus a new blocking `integration-enrolment-check` CI job (mirrors the `actions-pin-check` / `openapi-drift-check` self-contained meta-lint shape: unconditional, sub-second, pure bash + grep, no `changes.code` gate). The guard greps `internal/` for `//go:build integration`, derives the set of package directories, and diffs it against the `./internal/<pkg>/...` entries enumerated in the integration job's "Run integration tests" `go test` invocation; it fails (naming the offending package) when a tagged package is enrolled in neither the `ci.yml` list nor the script's `KNOWN_UNENROLLED` allowlist. This closes slice 334 framework-audit finding I-1 — the gap that lets an `integration_test.go` ship and silently run no integration tests in CI (the empirical cost being the 17-slice retroactive-enrolment trail: 279, 283, 284, 287, 288, 290, 293, 294, 295, 297, 310, 313, 315, 317, 318, 319, 320). Building the guard surfaced the live state it was designed to catch: **38 packages carry the build tag but are absent from the `ci.yml` list** (e.g. `internal/api/oauth` with 28 integration test functions, `internal/exception` with 22, `internal/auth/oidc`), confirming slice 348's independent `excludes` audit. Per anti-criterion P0-345-1 (no retroactive enrolment here), the 38 are recorded in the `KNOWN_UNENROLLED` allowlist as a documented, dated, monotonic-shrink ratchet; draining them is spillover slice 390. The guard still fails on the **next** forgotten package. Companion self-test `scripts/audit-integration-enrolment_test.sh` (synthetic positive + negative fixtures, 12 assertions) runs as the first step of the CI job. The integration job's package list is **unchanged** by this slice (AC-4); no test file is modified (P0-345-2); `CLAUDE.md` / canvas untouched (P0-345-3). Documents the rule in `CONTRIBUTING.md` ("Integration-test enrolment": ship `integration_test.go`, also add to the `ci.yml` integration list) and adds a `just audit-integration-enrolment` task. **Type: AFK** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/345-ci-integration-enrolment-discovery-decisions.md` (D1 shape: standalone shell script per `audit-rls.sh` precedent; D2 the known-gaps allowlist + slice-390 spillover; D3 normalization keying on the `internal/` segment; D4 blocking-not-advisory). Slice doc: `docs/issues/345-ci-integration-job-enrolment-discovery.md`.

### Performance

* **perf: slice 381 — perf cleanup round 1 (closes the slice 332 LOW-finding bundle, 6 sub-findings).** Bundles six mechanically-verifiable Low/Informational performance findings from the slice 332 audit, each landing as its own commit so a reviewer can revert one without losing the others (P0-1). **F-ING-2** (`internal/evidence/ingest/ingest.go`): the per-reject best-effort `writeAudit` tx ran on an unbounded `context.WithoutCancel` detached context; wrapped it in a 3-second `context.WithTimeout` (matching the slice-188 best-effort audit pattern) so a reject storm against a saturated pool fails the audit write fast rather than stacking connect-attempts — the verdict is already reached, so a timed-out audit write drops silently; slice-015 invariant order (size-check → schema-validate → redact → hash → write) untouched. **F-UCF-2** (`internal/api/ucfcoverage/`): split the 932-LOC `handlers.go` per-endpoint into `requirement_coverage.go`, `anchor_requirements.go`, and `control_coverage.go`, leaving the package-shared scaffolding (Handler, constructors, RegisterRoutes, lookup/tx helpers, wire types, JSON helpers) in `handlers.go`; move-and-rename only, zero semantic change. **F-OAUTH-2** (`internal/auth/tokensign`): `Sign` constructed a fresh `jose.NewSigner` (~235ns / 10 allocs) on every call; now memoised per active KeyID via `sync.Map` (P0-3: no new caching framework), keyed on KeyID so the slice-366 rotation overlap window caches each active key independently; a `Reset()` method empties the cache as the invalidation hook a future `keystore.Rotate` caller invokes. `BenchmarkSignerCachedVsUncached` isolates the acquisition step: cached 8.9 ns/op (0 allocs) vs uncached 235 ns/op (10 allocs), well under the AC-7 < 50% bar — the full-Sign total cannot meet that literal bar because the ES256 P-256 scalar multiplication (~20µs) dominates and is identical on both paths (decisions log D2). **F-OAUTH-3** (`internal/auth/keystore/fsstore`): `Get` did a per-call `make+copy` of the `[]VerificationKey` — an allocation on every JWT-bearing request since `Verify` hits `Get`; replaced the RWMutex-guarded signing/verify fields with an immutable snapshot published via `sync/atomic.Pointer`, so `Get` is now a lock-free pointer load returning the shared, never-mutated verify slice directly; mutators (load/generate/Rotate/Prune) serialise on a dedicated `loadMu` and swap a fresh snapshot atomically; slice-366 rotation/overlap/prune contract preserved, `-race` clean on the Rotate-during-Verify test. **F-OTEL-2**: new operator runbook `docs/operator/observability-tuning.md` documents the `OTEL_TRACES_SAMPLER=parentbased_traceidratio` + `OTEL_TRACES_SAMPLER_ARG=0.1` recipe under a "High DB query rate" header (documentation-only, P0-4 — sampler default unchanged), cross-linked from `docs/SELF_HOSTING.md`; the runbook notes that the shipped default is already the ratio sampler (the audit's "parentbased_always_on" premise was a stale reading of the slice 121 trail — decisions log D3). **F-ING-3** (`internal/canonjson`): added `BenchmarkHashRecordAtMaxPayload` + `TestHashRecord_AtMaxPayloadUnderBudget` locking the 1 MiB-payload SHA-256 cost as a regression gate, so an accidental O(payload²) re-canonicalisation or per-byte allocation blowup trips CI rather than silently eroding the 50ms ingest ack SLO. The test is a coarse **pathological-regression** gate — median-of-9 (warmup discarded) against a generous 100ms ceiling that sits 14-125× above any realistic CI sample (~1-7ms) yet far below any superlinear pathology (hundreds of ms to seconds), so it never flakes on a noisy shared runner; the `testing.B` benchmark remains the precise-number artifact (~441µs/op, 14 allocs). **Type: JUDGMENT** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/381-perf-cleanup-round-1-decisions.md` (D1 F-UCF-2 do-now split per AC-3 over the audit's defer-until-4th-endpoint framing; D2 AC-7 benchmark reframed to acquisition-isolation since the literal full-Sign < 50% bar is physically unreachable; D3 F-OTEL-2 corrects the audit's stale default-sampler premise; D4 F-OAUTH-3 snapshot model over per-call copy; D5 F-ING-3 pathological-regression ceiling + median-of-9 measurement after an initial 5ms single-sample ceiling flaked on CI). Slice doc: `docs/issues/381-perf-cleanup-round-1.md`.

* **perf(web): slice 380 — dashboard Server Component fan-out + parallel data fetch (closes slice 332 F-BFF-2 MEDIUM).** The `/dashboard` page's six panels (framework-posture, top-risks, freshness, drift, upcoming, activity) each fetched client-side via TanStack Query `useQuery` on cold load, paying their own bearer-cookie-read + Next.js BFF hop + upstream HTTP — a 6-7× per-load request amplification (slice 332 surface 5, finding F-BFF-2). A new sibling server-component `web/app/(authed)/dashboard/layout.tsx` now reads the `atlas_jwt` cookie once server-side and fans out all six panels' upstream fetches in parallel via `Promise.all` (`prefetchDashboard` in `web/app/(authed)/dashboard/dashboard-prefetch.ts`), seeding a per-request `QueryClient` under the EXACT keys the page's `useQuery` hooks register, then ships the dehydrated cache in the initial HTML via `<HydrationBoundary>`. The page's `useQuery` hooks boot already-populated, so a cold first load fires ZERO `/api/dashboard/**` BFF requests (AC-4/AC-8) — the user pays one network round-trip (the HTML document) instead of N. This generalizes slice 249's single-query `/settings` prefetch precedent to a six-query fan-out. The per-panel BFF routes REMAIN as the client-side refresh surface (P0-1, unremoved); their wire shape is unchanged (P0-4); the bearer is read server-side and never reaches the client (P0-3); `web/lib/api.ts apiFetch` now sets `cache: "no-store"` so the SSR fan-out never caches a tenant's posture across requests (P0-2). Prefetch fails soft per panel (`setQueryData` only on success — never seeds an error state, so a slow/failing upstream leaves that one panel unseeded and the client `useQuery` re-fetches it cold rather than hydrating into an error). New vitest `web/app/(authed)/dashboard/dashboard-prefetch.test.ts` (11 cases) pins query-key parity with the page, bearer-forwarding (P0-3), fail-soft fan-out (D3), and missing-bearer no-op; new Playwright `web/e2e/dashboard-server-component.spec.ts` asserts zero `/api/dashboard/*` requests on first load, full-panel content render, and that the BFF refresh surface still serves a 200 with the unchanged envelope. Per-file vitest coverage floor added for the new module (98/98/98/98). **Constitutional invariants honored**: tenant isolation unchanged — the platform derives tenant from the bearer credential server-side; the SC path uses the same bearer-cookie + upstream fetch shape as the BFF routes. **Type: JUDGMENT** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/380-dashboard-server-component-fanout-decisions.md` (D1 slice-249 prefetch pattern over pure-RSC; D2 per-panel TanStack state satisfies AC-2 Suspense intent; D3 fail-soft via `setQueryData`-on-success; D4 no explicit `Cache-Control` header — `cache:"no-store"` on the fetch suffices). Slice doc: `docs/issues/380-dashboard-server-component-fanout.md`.

* **perf(ingest): slice 379 — single marshal on redaction path (closes slice 332 F-ING-1 MEDIUM).** `internal/evidence/ingest/ingest.go Service.Process` now routes the marshal-of-record on the redaction-bearing code path through a new private `marshalLedger func(proto.Message) ([]byte, error)` field on `Service`, defaulted in `New()` to `protojson.Marshal`. The pre-redact `protojson.Marshal(rec.GetPayload())` call STAYS in place (its bytes serve size-check and schema-validation, per slice 015 D2 invariant order: size-check → schema-validate → redact → hash → write) but is now explicitly documented as a discardable throwaway when redaction rules apply. The post-redact marshal — the ONE marshal whose bytes are retained for the JSONB ledger column AND feed the canonjson hash — is the only call routed through the seam. New unit test `TestProcess_RedactionPath_LedgerMarshalCountIsOne` swaps in a counting wrapper and asserts the seam fires exactly once on the redaction-bearing path (AC-1); `BenchmarkIngestRedactionPath` asserts `ledgerCalls.Load() == int64(b.N)` as a CI canary (AC-8). Companion guard `TestProcess_NoRedactionPath_LedgerMarshalCountIsZero` confirms the no-rules path is unchanged (single marshal — already optimal — and the seam never fires when no rules apply). `TestProcess_RedactionApplied_BytesAreRedacted` asserts the ledger-bound bytes contain `<<REDACTED>>` AND do NOT contain the original secret value (P0-2 anti-criterion guard). One-line defensive nil-pool guard added to `writeAudit` so the same-package marshal-count tests can short-circuit at the seam without spinning up a real `pgxpool.Pool` (production `New()` panics on nil pool — unreachable in production). **Constitutional invariants honored**: invariant #2 (ingest/eval separation — refactor stays wholly inside `internal/evidence/ingest`; the redactor's proto-in/proto-out API at `internal/evidence/redact/redact.go` is untouched, P0-1); slice 015 D2 invariant order preserved verbatim (P0-4); P0-2 unredacted-bytes-never-logged-on-error-path preserved (the post-redact marshal error surfaces "payload re-marshal after redact" with no payload content). **Out-of-scope (intentional)**: F-ING-2 audit-write tx fan-out (bundled into slice 381); F-ING-3 canonjson CPU (informational only); a future slice can convert the redactor to in-place mutation if a structural CPU win on the redaction path is needed — slice 379's seam makes that future collapse mechanical (drop the pre-redact marshal, AC-1 assertion remains valid). **AC-3 slice-doc typo flagged**: AC-3 ("schema-validation hook receives the redacted payload bytes") directly contradicts P0-4 (canonical slice 015 D2 order). Resolution per slice prompt: preserve P0-4, treat AC-3 as a typo, recommend post-merge slice-doc patch. See decisions log D2 for full reasoning. Decisions log: `docs/audit-log/379-ingest-redaction-single-marshal-decisions.md` (D1 marshal-count interpretation; D2 AC-3 typo resolution; D3 same-package test seam placement; D4 sentinel-error short-circuit + nil-pool guard; D5 benchmark shape; D6 no-rules-path guard branch; D7 defensive byte-copy; D8 no interface widening; D9 explicit non-touches; D10 STATUS row left to orchestrator). Slice doc: `docs/issues/379-ingest-redaction-single-marshal.md`.

* **feat(authz): slice 378 — hot-reload authz bundle without server restart (closes slice 332 F-OPA-2 HIGH).** `internal/authz/decision.go` now stores the prepared OPA query behind a `sync/atomic.Pointer[rego.PreparedEvalQuery]` and exposes `(*authz.Engine).Reload(ctx, modules, sources, validator)` + `ReloadFromEmbedded(ctx, validator)` so the embedded `policies/authz/*.rego` bundle can be reloaded without restarting the atlas binary. The atomic-pointer contract is the entire load-bearing piece: a concurrent `Decide()` call during a `Reload()` sees EITHER the old query OR the new one — never a partial state. The pre-swap matrix gate is the second load-bearing piece: a NEW production-code file `internal/authz/matrix_validator.go` exports `CanonicalMatrix()` (33-row role × endpoint table mirroring the slice 026 integration test) and `ValidateMatrix(ctx, candidate)` that evaluates every cell against the CANDIDATE prepared query BEFORE `storeQuery`. Matrix-failure aborts the reload — the engine continues to serve the prior bundle (slice 378 AC-3). New maintainer-only HTTP endpoint `POST /v1/admin/authz-bundle/reload` wired at `internal/api/adminauthzbundle/`: super_admin-gated (`jwtmw.FromContext().SuperAdmin` is the first check; the OPA `super_admin.rego` is the upstream second leg), per-actor rate-limited at 1 reload per 60s, audit-log-dual-write on success (one `super_admin_audit_log` row + one `me_audit_log` row inside a single transaction; both carry `{before_bundle_sha256, after_bundle_sha256}` in payload). Migration `20260528000000_authz_bundle_reload_meta_audit.sql` extends the CHECK constraints on `me_audit_log.action` AND `super_admin_audit_log.action` to admit `'authz_bundle_reload'` (strict superset of the slice-278 baseline). Coverage: race test `TestReload_RaceConcurrentDecideAndReload` (16 deciders × 4 reloaders × 250ms under `-race`; zero Decide errors required); `TestReload_ValidatorRunsAgainstNewQuery` asserts the matrix runs against the CANDIDATE not the live query (slice doc note 2 — common-bug-shape defence); `TestReload_ValidatorFailureRejected` asserts the engine continues to serve the prior bundle on validator failure; `TestReload_ValidateMatrixOnEmbeddedBundlePasses` asserts the production validator passes against the embedded bundle (canonical-bundle drift detector); handler unit tests cover 403 / 503 / 422 / 429 paths; integration tests cover happy-path dual-write + non-super_admin 403 + matrix-failure 422 + rate-limit 429. **Constitutional invariants honored:** invariant #6 (RLS tenant isolation — me_audit_log row anchored to the actor's session tenant; super_admin_audit_log is platform-global per slice 142 D1); append-only audit ledger (canvas §4.3 — the migration adds an action value, never alters existing rows); AI-assist boundary unchanged (this is a runtime substrate change; no AI-assist surface touched). **Out-of-scope (intentional):** v3+ per-tenant custom-control bundles (canvas §4.4 — slice 378 P0-4); regocache touches (slice 377's domain — P0-378-5); distributed rate-limit backend (v2 atlas-edge multi-binary follow-up). **Engineer-as-collaborator gap surface:** §D10 (matrix-vs-test lockstep) + §D4 (target_user_id contract bend on platform-global event — future v2 schema cleanup) + §D5 (distributed limiter for v2 atlas-edge) + §D4 (audit-write failure recovery via background retry) consolidate the substrate gaps for maintainer attention. **Slice 332 F-OPA-2 closure path:** the v1 "restart-required" deferral is now retired; v2 atlas-edge multi-tenant rollout is de-risked. Decisions log: `docs/audit-log/378-authz-bundle-hot-reload-decisions.md` (D1 empty-body embedded-only request shape; D2 atomic.Pointer over RWMutex; D3 production-code matrix validator vs test-only refactor; D4 dual-write audit-log emission with target_user_id contract bend honestly named; D5 per-actor in-process rate limiter; D6 sorted-filename NUL-separated SHA-256 fingerprint; D7 separate modules + sources parameters for Reload; D8 new `adminauthzbundle` package vs extending `adminsuperadmins`; D9 explicit non-touches; D10 matrix-against-candidate-not-live contract). Slice doc: `docs/issues/378-authz-bundle-hot-reload.md`.

* **perf(eval): slice 377 — cache `rego.PreparedEvalQuery` in eval engine (closes slice 332 F-OPA-1 CRITICAL).** New `internal/eval/regocache` package generalises the prepare-once pattern already proven at `internal/authz/decision.go:60` and applies it to the two hot-path call sites that the slice 332 performance audit identified as re-preparing per call: `internal/eval/rego.go evalRegoQuery` (evidence-query sandbox; called once per `(control × scope_cell)` inside `EvaluateAll`) and `internal/risk/aggrule/severity.go evalCustomRego` (custom_rego severity policies). Cache key = SHA-256(policy text) ⨁ SHA-256(sorted capability builtin names) ⨁ query ⨁ moduleName; sync.Map-backed (per slice doc note 1); package-level instance per call site (D4); OTel `atlas_eval_regocache_hits_total` / `atlas_eval_regocache_misses_total` counters emit lazily via slice 121's global MeterProvider. **Measured delta** (`Apple M3 Ultra darwin/arm64`, `-benchtime=2s`): `evalRegoQuery` 225,498 ns/op → **31,951 ns/op** (**7.06× faster**); allocations 4,207/op → 273/op (**15.4× reduction**); bytes 200,168 B/op → 21,349 B/op (**9.4× reduction**). At v1 scale (200 active controls × ~3 scope cells per control = ~600 calls per `EvaluateAll` tick): **pure-CPU savings ~116 ms per scheduled-eval tick (86% reduction from ~135 ms → ~19 ms)**. **Out-of-scope (intentional):** `internal/authz/decision.go` left untouched (P0-377-4 — already the reference pattern); LRU eviction deferred per D1 (v1 policy population bounded by control catalog ~200 entries, fits in process memory); per-meter-name labelling deferred per D4 footnote (operator dashboards can already filter on otel_scope_name). **Constitutional invariants honored:** invariant #2 (separated ingest/eval stages — cache lives wholly in the eval stage); invariant #6 (tenant isolation — cache key is policy-text-derived NOT tenant-derived; two tenants authoring identical policy text share the cached compiled AST which holds no eval result, by construction no cross-tenant data leak); AI-assist boundary (cache is structural — does not change OPA evaluation semantics, P0-377-1). Decisions log: `docs/audit-log/377-rego-prepared-query-cache-decisions.md` (D1 unbounded sync.Map vs LRU; D2 risk/aggrule in-scope; D3 OTel counter shape; D4 per-package vs shared cache instance; D5 measured benchmark numbers). Slice doc: `docs/issues/377-eval-rego-prepared-query-cache.md`.

* **docs(adr): slice 400 — OSCAL cosign/Sigstore signing decision spike + ADR (368 go/no-go).** Decision-only spike (no production code, slice 400 P0-400-1) gating slice 368's ~5d cosign-migration build. Filed [`docs/adr/0010-oscal-cosign-signing.md`](docs/adr/0010-oscal-cosign-signing.md) (next sequential ADR slot; 0003 double-occupancy untouched). **Recommendation: ADOPT-DEFERRED, confidence HIGH.** Adopt cosign as the committed direction for signing OSCAL audit-export bundles (distinct from slice 084's already-cosign-signed release binaries / container images — runtime-export signing is a different artifact + a different identity), and re-scope slice 368 into two phased sub-slices: **368a (Phase 1, ~3d)** — `internal/oscal/cosign` wrapper + `cosign-kms` mode + retained `embedded-ed25519` + mode dispatch + backward-compat + CLI + runbook + Mode-A/B integration tests; **no Fulcio/Rekor/OIDC dependency**, closes the bulk of the named auditor friction (ad-hoc embedded key + bespoke verifier) with stock `cosign verify-blob`; and **368b (Phase 2, ~2d, gated)** — `cosign-keyless` + Fulcio + Rekor transparency log, blocked on a separate OIDC-identity-strategy decision. **Load-bearing finding:** `cosign-keyless` via atlas's own AS (slice 188 `client_credentials`) does NOT work against public Fulcio as 368 proposed — slice 188 mints a per-deployment, non-public issuer that is not in Fulcio's federated trust root; keyless needs a public IdP, a private Sigstore stack, or Sigstore-root onboarding first. **cosign license finding:** cosign is Apache-2.0; bundling the unmodified binary is license-clean (permits binary redistribution; compatible with both candidate project licenses; preserve `LICENSE`+`NOTICE`, pin the version, record provenance in asset-inventory §2.3) — P0-368-4 satisfied. **Per-deployment defaults:** air-gap self-host → `embedded-ed25519` (only reachable mode; non-negotiable); connected self-host with KMS → `cosign-kms`; SaaS → `cosign-kms` at GA (revises slice 368 AC-9's `cosign-keyless` default), keyless after Phase 2. Slice 368 re-scoped (`docs/issues/368-cosign-signing-migration.md`): status `ready` → `blocked` on ADR-0010 sign-off, "Re-scoped by ADR-0010" section added with the day-by-day → 368a/368b mapping, AC-8 marked done (recorded in ADR-0010), AC-9 revised. **Does NOT auto-merge** (slice 400 P0-400-2) — the PR is the maintainer's decision gate. * **docs(audit): slice 332 — performance audit (evidence pipeline + UCF + OPA + OAuth + frontend + observability) via voltagent-qa-sec:performance-engineer persona.** Read-only audit of `main@eec5a2d0` across six load-bearing performance surfaces: (1) evidence ingest pipeline (`internal/evidence/ingest` + slice-015 NATS JetStream substrate), (2) UCF graph traversal (`internal/api/ucfcoverage` two-hop JOIN, baselined against slice 008's 5.89 ms mean / 5.88 ms p50 / 6.91 ms p95 — 34× under the 200 ms target), (3) OPA evaluation (`internal/eval/rego.go` evidence-query sandbox + `internal/authz/decision.go` request-time authz), (4) OAuth substrate (`internal/api/oauth` token endpoint + `internal/auth/tokensign` ES256 sign/verify), (5) frontend BFF route handlers (`web/app/api/*/route.ts` + `web/lib/api/bff.ts`), (6) observability stack overhead (`internal/observability/otel` SDK + `otelpgx`). **Methodology: static-analysis + benchmark-test reading + decisions-log citation** — live load generation deferred per slice's "Notes for the implementing agent" explicit authorization (D4 captures the JUDGMENT). **Headline finding:** **F-OPA-1 (CRITICAL)** — `internal/eval/rego.go evalRegoQuery` calls `rego.New(...).PrepareForEval(ctx)` on every `computeRow` invocation; with 200 active controls × modest cell fan-out, the eval engine pays 200+ OPA compiles per scheduled-eval tick. The correct pattern (prepare-once + store `rego.PreparedEvalQuery`) already exists in the same codebase at `internal/authz/decision.go:60`. A second site of the same anti-pattern lives at `internal/risk/aggrule/severity.go:134`. **Findings:** 1 Critical · 1 High · 3 Medium · 6 Low · 4 Informational = 15 total across the 6 surfaces. **Spillover follow-ups filed (cap 5):** **377** (F-OPA-1 — cache `rego.PreparedEvalQuery` per policy text in eval engine + risk aggrule), **378** (F-OPA-2 — hot-reload authz bundle without server restart; HIGH escalates from "v1 deferred" to "must-fix-before-v2"), **379** (F-ING-1 — eliminate double `protojson.Marshal` on ingest redaction path; operator-visible at sustained >100 RPS on redaction-bearing kinds), **380** (F-BFF-2 — dashboard Server Component fan-out + parallel data fetch; collapses 7+ BFF round-trips per page-load into 1), **381** (perf cleanup round 1 — bundles 6 Low/Info findings: F-ING-2 reject-path audit tx timeout, F-UCF-2 handlers.go split, F-OAUTH-2 cached `jose.Signer`, F-OAUTH-3 immutable verification-key handle, F-OTEL-2 sampler-tuning operator runbook, F-ING-3 canonjson hash CPU benchmark regression gate). F-BFF-3 (`web/lib/api.ts` 2901 LOC) is NOT a new finding — already covered by slice 370. **Surfaces flagged healthy:** UCF graph traversal (slice 008 baseline preserved by unchanged schema + index shape; 5.89 ms mean / 6.91 ms p95 still holds at the benchmark fixture scale); ingest core path (Service.Process boundary holds constitutional invariant #3); OAuth ES256 sign/verify path (go-jose performance acceptable); OTel no-op default (genuine zero-cost when `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT` unset per slice 121 AC-2). **Severity rubric applied (D2):** Critical = >2× regression OR operator-visible on v1-binary-criterion hot path; High = 1.5–2× OR structural pattern that will become Critical at v2 scale; Medium = noticeable inefficiency at >100 RPS sustained; Low = codebase-onboarding observation; Informational = healthy steady-state or design-intent. **Regression-vs-baseline threshold (D3):** literal application of slice doc's >2× rule, ENRICHED with the in-codebase-correct-pattern criterion (F-OPA-1 has no published baseline but is structurally wrong vs. authz Engine; severity CRITICAL notwithstanding the absence of a fabricated benchmark number). **Spillover cap-5 triage (D5):** Critical / High → own slice always; Medium → own slice if isolated; Low → bundle into "perf cleanup round 1"; Informational → audit-report-only; final count 4 individual + 1 bundle = 5, cap honored. **Constitutional invariants honored** — invariant #2 (separated ingest/eval) verified; invariant #6 (RLS tenant isolation) unchanged; invariant #3 (append-only ledger) verified by F-OAUTH-3 + F-OPA-1 remediation paths not crossing the ledger boundary. **Adjacent observations** (NOT slice 332 findings; named in PR body only for orchestrator visibility): (a) `internal/eval/engine.go loadEvidence` is unbounded in record count per control — v2 re-shape; (b) slice 371 just landed clock injection across auth substrate — extending to eval engine would let slice 377's prepared-query cache be tested deterministically. **P0 anti-criteria honored:** P0-332-1 NO load against atlas-edge or production (static-analysis path only); P0-332-2 NO auto-merge; P0-332-3 NO code modified (audit diff = doc files only, decisions log D10 verifies); P0-332-4 NO PII / customer screenshots; P0-332-5 NO touches to CLAUDE.md or canvas; P0-332-6 NO new perf-testing framework dependency; P0-332-7 NO production load tests. **Engineer-as-collaborator gap surface:** report's "Adjacent observations" section + decisions log §D6 consolidate the items that fell outside slice 332's scope but deserve maintainer attention. **Slice doc status flipped `ready` → `in-review`.** Audit report at `docs/audits/332-performance-audit-report.md`; decisions log at `docs/audit-log/332-performance-audit-decisions.md`; spillover slice docs at `docs/issues/377-eval-rego-prepared-query-cache.md`, `docs/issues/378-authz-bundle-hot-reload.md`, `docs/issues/379-ingest-redaction-single-marshal.md`, `docs/issues/380-dashboard-server-component-fanout.md`, `docs/issues/381-perf-cleanup-round-1.md`.

* **audit(compliance): slice 329 — compliance meta-audit via voltagent-qa-sec:compliance-auditor persona.** Read-only operator-side gap analysis of v1-complete `main` at HEAD `bb9d0adc` (post-slice-371 reconcile) against SOC 2 Trust Services Criteria (Security + Availability + Confidentiality), ISO 27001:2022 Annex A (5.x organizational + 8.x technological controls), NIST CSF 2.0 (six functions: Govern + Identify + Protect + Detect + Respond + Recover), GDPR Articles 25/30/32 (Art 33 deferred per OQ #10), HIPAA Security Rule (164.308 administrative + 164.312 technical safeguards; 164.310 physical N/A SaaS), and PCI DSS v4.0 non-CDE scope (req 6/8/10/11/12 only). **This is a gap analysis, not a certification claim** — security-atlas is not SOC 2 certified, not ISO 27001 certified, not HIPAA-attested; the audit examines whether the project's evidence could pass those audits today. **Headline finding:** technical controls (auth substrate, RLS tenant isolation, CI scanner coverage, change management discipline) are exceptionally strong; the operator-side gaps are **organizational and operational** — the policy artifacts a third-party reviewer expects to see before examining technical evidence. **No Critical findings.** 5 High (H-1 no documented Incident Response plan — most-load-bearing for v1 binary success criterion; H-2 no documented Business Continuity / Disaster Recovery plan; H-3 no documented GitHub-org access review cadence; H-4 no documented data retention + disposal policy; H-5 no project-level asset inventory document), 6 Medium (M-1 project-level monitoring SLOs; M-2 change-mgmt policy consolidation; M-3 vendor mgmt register; M-4 personnel security policy stub deferred per solo-maintainer stage; M-5 promotion policy formalization; M-6 project risk register), 4 Low (L-1 CoC reporting placeholder; L-2 SECURITY-ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS.md forward reference; L-3 project-side observability gap; L-4 CHANGELOG audit-trail formalization), 8 Informational (strong slice-process audit trail, branch-protection ruleset, CI scanner coverage, DCO discipline; plus correctly-deferred items: GDPR Art 33 per OQ #10, privacy v0 per OQ #7, HIPAA per-customer-scope to FrameworkScope, PCI DSS N/A no CDE). **Spillover follow-ups filed (cap 5):** **372** (H-1 — Incident Response plan), **373** (H-2 — Business Continuity / DR plan), **374** (H-3 — GitHub org access review cadence), **375** (H-4 — Data retention + disposal policy), **376** (H-5 — Project asset inventory). All 6 Mediums kept audit-report-only per JUDGMENT D3 — they share the structural cause "no consolidated compliance evidence index" that the 5 Highs collectively close. Zero findings duplicate slices 327 (security audit) or 328 (code review); cross-references recorded for ISO 27001 8.24 cryptography (slice 366 key rotation) and 8.31 supply-chain integrity (slice 368 cosign migration). Per-framework readiness verdicts: SOC 2 + ISO 27001 NO-pre-readiness with strong technical controls; NIST CSF PARTIAL (Identify + Respond + Recover gaps); GDPR PARTIAL Art 32 only; HIPAA + PCI DSS N/A. ### Quality

* **test(e2e): slice 394 — load `/e2e/` `route.fulfill` mocks from contract goldens (closes slice 392 D5 deferral; resolves slice 334 P-1 for the golden-covered routes).** The Playwright e2e suite hand-wrote upstream response bodies in `route.fulfill` calls (slice 334 finding P-1), which can silently drift from the provider's recorded wire shape — the slice-210 / slice-276 class of bug ADR-0007's contract tier exists to catch. Slices 349/392 + 409 recorded the real Go handler bodies into `web/lib/contracts/*.golden.json` for nine endpoints; this slice teaches the e2e mocks for those routes to load from the goldens. **New helper** `web/e2e/test-utils/fulfill-from-golden.ts`: `fulfillFromGolden(route, endpoint, variant, { status?, override? })` reads a golden and serves the recorded body via `route.fulfill`. `endpoint` is a typed `GoldenEndpoint` union of the nine covered routes (`me`, `version`, `install-state`, `demo-status`, `framework-posture`, `activity`, `upcoming`, `freshness`, `drift`) — a typo cannot fall through to a non-golden path; an unknown `variant` throws (listing the available keys). The caller keeps `page.route(pattern, …)` + any method-guard; the helper owns only the fulfill. **Specs migrated** (every spec hand-writing a body for a golden-covered route): `first-time-login.spec.ts` (two install-state mocks → `fresh_install_without_tenant` / `post_first_install`), `dashboard.spec.ts` slice-229 subtitle tests (freshness `populated`+override for the deterministic 87% + two `empty`-variant cases), `settings-profile-credential-bearer.spec.ts` + `settings-notifications-credential-bearer.spec.ts` (`/api/me` → `synthetic_admin` + `display_name` override). **Left hand-mocked by design:** error/abort paths (no recorded body — the AC-3 escape hatch, e.g. the install-state 503 fallback + the dashboard `abort()` degrade tests), and routes with no golden (`/v1/risks`, `/v1/controls/*`, `/v1/board`, `/v1/policies` — goldens tracked as #410 / #411); the typed union mechanically prevents passing an uncovered endpoint. **Escape hatch (AC-3)** documented in `web/e2e/README.md` "Golden-backed route mocks" and tested two ways: the credential-bearer + freshness specs exercise the `override` deep-merge (golden stays the shape-complete base; only the assertion-load-bearing value changes), and the install-state spec keeps its hand-written 503 path beside the golden path. **Helper self-test** `web/lib/contracts/fulfill-from-golden.test.ts` pins the pure logic (endpoint→file map, variant lookup, unknown-variant throw, override merge) on the existing vitest surface (the helper's only Playwright import is `import type { Route }`, erased at runtime). **Zero new tooling, zero new CI job, zero new gate** (AC-4) — rides the existing `Frontend · Playwright e2e` + `Frontend · vitest` surfaces; `.github/workflows/ci.yml` untouched. **Type: JUDGMENT** — decisions log `docs/audit-log/394-e2e-fulfill-from-golden-decisions.md` (D1 helper shape + location; D2 migration inventory; D3 escape hatch; D4 zero-new-gate; D5 the discourage-new-hand-mocks note). ADR: `docs/adr/0007-contract-test-tier.md`. Slice doc: `docs/issues/394-e2e-mocks-load-from-contract-goldens.md`.
