## [Unreleased]

### Added

- Risk register data export
  ([#136](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/136); spillover
  from slice 135). New `GET /v1/risks/export?format=<csv|json|xlsx>`
  endpoint dumps the full risk register for the authenticated tenant in
  CSV, JSON, or XLSX. Reuses the slice 135 data-export library and
  inherits the slice 145 per-(tenant, user) concurrency cap. Canonical
  18-column set covers id / title / description / category / methodology
  / treatment / treatment_owner / accepter / instrument_reference /
  inherent_score / residual_score / severity / org_unit_id / themes /
  review_due_at / accepted_until / created_at / updated_at —
  `treatment_narrative` is intentionally excluded at v1 (slice 136
  P0-A-Risk-1; defer to a future column-selection slice). Row cap
  defaults to 50,000 risks. Meta-audit action is `risk_export` (distinct
  from `audit_log_export` so forensic queries can enumerate
  risk-register extractions separately). BFF at `/api/risks/export`
  forwards the bearer-only auth to the platform. Risk-register page
  ships three Export buttons (CSV / JSON / XLSX) replacing the prior
  disabled placeholder. Migration `20260519000010_risk_export_meta_audit`
  extends the `me_audit_log.action` CHECK to permit the new value. See
  `docs/audit-log/136-risk-register-export-decisions.md` for the
  column-set rationale and the audit-period-freezing decision
  (D2 — risks have no observed_at; the per-period attested state lives
  in the slice 028 attestation workflow, not the export endpoint).
- Audit-log export: payload-redaction flag + per-(tenant, user)
  concurrency cap
  ([#145](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/145);
  retro-STRIDE follow-on from slice 135). `GET /v1/admin/audit-log/export`
  gains `?include_payload=<bool>` (default `true` — preserves slice 135
  wire shape). When `false`, CSV emits an empty cell, JSON emits the
  literal `null`, and XLSX emits an empty cell for the `payload_json`
  column; all other columns render normally (slice 145 P0-A2 keeps
  column-level redaction beyond `payload_json` out of scope). The
  meta-audit row records the value used (legacy slice 135 rows without
  the key represent default-true). NEW `internal/export/concurrency.go`
  ships a per-(tenant, user) semaphore (default cap 2, tunable via
  `ATLAS_EXPORT_MAX_CONCURRENT_PER_USER`); excess returns 429 with
  `Retry-After: 30` header AND a JSON body explaining the limit
  (P0-A10 — operators reading curl without `-i` still see the message).
  The cap is per-tenant-per-user, not global — a super_admin running
  exports across five tenants is NOT throttled by cap=2 in any single
  tenant. CONTRIBUTING.md gains a "Data exports" section covering both
  workflows (forensics default + external-audit-handoff with
  `?include_payload=false`). Decisions log at
  `docs/audit-log/145-data-export-hardening-decisions.md`.

- Personal API tokens: Rotate action on /settings
  ([#163](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/163); closes
  slice 154 F8). The Personal API Tokens table in
  `/settings#tokens` gains a Rotate button per row, mirroring the
  /admin/api-keys rotate flow (slice 062). The `token-state.ts` reducer
  is extended with a `ROTATED` transition carrying
  `{bearer, last4, predecessor_last4, predecessor_expires_at}`; the
  plaintext-once invariant (P0-163-1) applies symmetrically with ISSUED
  — DISMISS clears the bearer, any subsequent ISSUED/ROTATED replaces
  the prior one regardless of which path produced it. A new
  `RotateConfirmModal` mirrors `RevokeConfirmModal` with copy
  explaining that the predecessor row stays visible with a muted
  `rotated → …{last4}` badge until separately revoked (slice 062
  D-062-3). The `FreshTokenCallout` is widened to a discriminated-union
  prop so the same component renders both issue-flavour and
  rotate-flavour copy. The successor-link badge is derived from the
  slice 062 `rotated_from` field on the successor row (the slice doc
  mistakenly named the inverse direction `superseded_by` — see D3 in
  the decisions log for the wire-shape reconciliation). Pure-frontend
  wiring: no backend or BFF route change (P0-163-2/P0-163-3). Decisions
  log at
  `docs/audit-log/163-settings-api-tokens-rotate-action-decisions.md`.

- Active sessions show user-agent, IP, and geo
  ([#162](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/162); closes
  slice 154 F6). The `sessions` table gains four nullable columns
  (`user_agent`, `ip_address`, `geo_country`, `geo_city`) via migration
  `20260518100000_sessions_augment_ua_ip_geo.sql` (idempotent / reversible).
  The user-facing OIDC + local-login session-create paths now capture the
  caller's `User-Agent` header (truncated to 512 bytes — DoS guard) and IP
  address (`r.RemoteAddr` by default, honoring `X-Forwarded-For` only when
  `TRUST_FORWARDED_HEADERS=1` per OWASP IP-spoofing guidance). The
  slice-108 `/v1/me/sessions` wire shape exposes the four new fields with
  `omitempty`, the slice-110 BFF route proxies them transparently
  (passthrough body), and the settings page Active Sessions section renders
  them as a `… · UA · IP · City, Country` line beneath the existing
  Created / last used line. Per anti-criterion P0-162-1 the line is
  rendered honestly: missing fields are omitted (no fabricated
  "(unknown)" placeholder), and rows with no augmented fields render
  identically to today. Geo enrichment (IP → country/city) is NOT in
  scope of this slice; the columns ship nullable and a follow-up
  populates them. Decisions log at
  `docs/audit-log/162-sessions-wire-shape-decisions.md`.

### Fixed

- **slice 184** — UI honesty: `/audits` row-click no longer 404s
  ([#184](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/184); closes
  slice-178 first-pass F-178-4 HONESTY-GAP). The audits-list page
  (`web/app/(authed)/audits/page.tsx`) previously rendered every
  audit-period row as a clickable target that pushed
  `/audits/{id}` — a route that does not exist and 404'd with the
  standard Next.js not-found UI. The slice-178 UI-honesty audit
  categorized this as a HONESTY-GAP: the live UI promised a
  per-period detail page that the codebase does not yet ship.
  This slice resolves the gap via Option A (per the slice 184
  doc): the `onRowClick` prop is removed from the `ListTable`,
  the `ListTable` primitive drops both the click handler and the
  `cursor-pointer` class when `onRowClick` is undefined, and a new
  shadcn `Alert` banner above the table
  (`data-testid="audits-detail-coming-soon-banner"`) surfaces the
  disclosure: "Per-period detail view is coming in a future slice."
  Option B (ship the actual detail page) was deferred to a separate
  slice once the detail-page UX is decided — see
  `docs/audit-log/184-audits-row-click-404-decisions.md` D1 for the
  trade-off. Playwright spec `web/e2e/audits-list.spec.ts` AC-7 is
  reversed (not deleted) — the spec now asserts the absence of
  `cursor-pointer`, the absence of navigation on click, and the
  presence of the banner; still quarantined behind the slice 082
  seed harness as before. No backend change, no data-contract
  change, no audit harness change (P0-184-2 / P0-184-3 honored).
  Decisions log:
  [`docs/audit-log/184-audits-row-click-404-decisions.md`](./docs/audit-log/184-audits-row-click-404-decisions.md).

- **slice 176** — Logo variant now follows app theme; README +
  `docs/images/` regenerated to match slice-167 design
  ([#176](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/176)).
  Two bugs:
  **Bug A** — the three logo mount sites
  (`web/components/shell/topbar.tsx`, `web/app/login/page.tsx`, and the
  audit row for `web/app/layout.tsx` which renders no `<img>`) used a
  `<picture media="(prefers-color-scheme: ...)">` element that tracked
  the OS preference, not the app theme picker (slice 070/170's
  persisted `data-theme` attribute on `<html>`). Operators on OS=dark
  with explicit app theme "light" were served `/logo-dark.svg`
  (near-white ink, `#f8fafc`) onto a light app background and could
  not see the logo at all. Replaced the inline `<picture>` blocks with
  a new `<ThemeAwareLogo>` component
  (`web/components/shell/theme-aware-logo.tsx`) that reads
  `<html data-theme>` directly + uses a `MutationObserver` to re-render
  on /settings changes + falls back to `prefers-color-scheme` only when
  the resolved theme is `"system"`. Pure picker logic
  (`web/lib/theme-aware-logo.ts`) is unit-tested in vitest covering all
  four (app-theme × OS-pref) combinations (8 tests).
  **Bug B** — `docs/images/logo-{light,dark}.png` were the pre-slice-167
  design (slice 167's anti-criterion P0-A4 limited that slice to
  `web/public/`, deferring the docs/README assets here). Regenerated
  both PNGs from the slice 167 SVG sources via the same sharp@0.34 +
  pngquant pipeline; the regenerated files end up byte-identical
  (SHA-256 matched) to `web/public/logo-{light,dark}.png` because both
  pipelines are deterministic for the same inputs. Both PNGs are 4638 B
  / 4746 B gzipped — well under the slice 167 STRIDE-D 16 KB cap.
  Playwright spec `web/e2e/logo-render.spec.ts` extended with a Bug A
  regression assertion: sets `<html data-theme="dark">` from a
  `page.evaluate()` and asserts the rendered `<img src>` flips to the
  dark variant; toggling back to `"light"` flips it back to the light
  variant regardless of OS preference. Decisions log at
  [`docs/audit-log/176-logo-theme-coupling-decisions.md`](docs/audit-log/176-logo-theme-coupling-decisions.md)
  (D1 = `data-theme` reader + MutationObserver pattern, chosen because
  slice 170 writes `data-theme` not a Tailwind `dark:` class; D2 =
  component named `ThemeAwareLogo` colocated at
  `web/components/shell/`; D3 = sharp + pngquant pipeline matching
  slice 167; D4 = AC-7 audit confirming `web/app/layout.tsx` renders no
  `<img>` — only Metadata API `icons` + OG/Twitter image URLs, none of
  which are theme-coupled at runtime).

- Playwright e2e: settings page coverage gated on CI
  ([#164](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/164); closes
  slice 154 F11). `web/e2e/settings.spec.ts` joins the gated CI rotation:
  the eleven AC bodies that have been preserved as commented contracts
  since slice 103 (AC-1..AC-6), slice 154 (AC-7..AC-10), and slice 163
  (AC-11) are now un-commented and exercised on every Playwright run.
  Adds `fixtures/e2e/settings.sql` seeding a real `users` row in the
  demo tenant (display name, non-default `time_zone =
  'America/New_York'`), two `user_roles` rows (`admin` + `grc_engineer`
  so the multi-role tail badge renders), one
  `user_notification_preferences` cell with `enabled=false`, two
  `sessions` rows (one with slice-162 UA/IP/geo populated, one bare to
  exercise the P0-162-1 honest-empty path), and a slice-062 predecessor
  → successor api_keys chain so the AC-9 table branch and AC-11 rotate
  chain have starting data. `web/e2e/seed.ts` learns a `"settings"`
  fixture name; `seedApiKey()` threads `issued_by = DEMO_USER_ID` into
  the admin bearer row for that fixture only (the five pre-existing
  fixtures keep the historical NULL behavior) so `/v1/me` resolves a
  real `users` row rather than falling into the synthetic-profile
  branch. The AC-3 body was reshaped from the slice 154 localStorage
  check to a server-round-trip check because slice 108 retired the
  localStorage fallback (the toggle is now server-of-truth via
  `PATCH /v1/me/preferences`); the original intent (the toggle persists)
  is preserved. Decisions log at
  `docs/audit-log/164-settings-e2e-seed-decisions.md`.

- Playwright `control-detail-empty.spec.ts` fixture file is now present
  ([#160](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/160)). Slice
  152 shipped `web/e2e/control-detail-empty.spec.ts` whose `beforeAll`
  calls `seedFromFixture("control-detail-empty")`, but the corresponding
  `fixtures/e2e/control-detail-empty.sql` file was never created. The
  `Frontend · Playwright e2e` CI job is gated by `dorny/paths-filter@v4`
  so this stayed latent across docs-only PRs between slice 152's merge
  and slice 153's PR #330 — slice 153 was the first PR whose file
  changes pushed the path filter into `code=true`, surfacing
  `Error: seed: fixture not found at .../fixtures/e2e/control-detail-empty.sql`.
  This slice adds the missing fixture as a tracer-bullet fix: the
  "empty state" the spec verifies IS the absence of inserts, so the
  fixture sets `app.current_tenant` to the slice-082 demo tenant
  (`00000000-0000-0000-0000-00000000d3a0`) and commits an empty
  transaction. The harness wiring works; the spec's commented
  assertions stay commented per slice 152's deferral to slice 112.
  `fixtures/e2e/README.md`'s per-spec table is updated to include both
  the new `control-detail-empty.sql` row and the pre-existing
  `audit-log.sql` row that was missing from the table.
- **quality:** auth-open-redirect Playwright spec drift
  ([#161](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/161)). The
  `web/e2e/auth-open-redirect.spec.ts` spec (slice 086 live-verification
  of the open-redirect HIGH remediation) has been silently failing on
  `main` since merge — slice 079's `continue-on-error: true` quarantine
  + a docs-only path filter on the `Frontend · Playwright e2e` job
  masked the failure until slice 153 PR #330 triggered the real job.
  JUDGMENT-type slice with 3-case diagnosis matrix (behavior regression
  / spec drift / fixture drift); evidence in the CI trace + failure
  artifacts ruled out Case 1 (host assertion at line 71 passed —
  open-redirect defense IS functional) and Case 3 (page-snapshot at
  failure time shows the dashboard fully rendered — fixture is producing
  a valid session). Case 2 selected: the spec's `waitForURL` predicate
  was self-referential —
  `(url) => url.origin === new URL(authedPage.url()).origin` resolved
  immediately because `authedPage.url()` returns the current page URL,
  so the candidate's origin was compared against itself (always true).
  `waitForURL` returned without actually waiting for the post-sign-in
  redirect; line 70's `final = new URL(authedPage.url())` then captured
  `/login?from=...` mid-flight and the pathname assertion fired. Fix
  replaces the predicate with `(url) => !url.pathname.startsWith("/login")`
  which actually waits for the redirect off `/login`. Smallest possible
  change — no edit to `web/lib/safe-redirect.ts` (P0-A1), no edit to
  `web/app/login/actions.ts` (Case 1 ruled out), no edit to
  `web/e2e/fixtures.ts` (Case 3 ruled out). Decisions log at
  `docs/audit-log/161-playwright-auth-open-redirect-spec-drift-decisions.md`
  records the diagnosis chain, alternatives rejected, and the
  revisit-once-in-use list (slice 141 multi-tenant, slice 034 OIDC RP,
  slice 116 promote-e2e). The open-redirect defense itself is unchanged
  and continues to be gated by the always-required
  `web/lib/safe-redirect.test.ts` vitest (9 cases, all green).
- Logo SVGs render correctly in production-build standalone
  ([#153](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/153)).
  Operators reported on v1.10.0 Unraid that the header logo + login-
  screen logo still didn't render even after slice 123's `proxy.ts`
  exempt-list fix landed. Root cause: the Next.js `output: "standalone"`
  tracer (`web/next.config.ts`) does NOT copy `web/public/` into the
  standalone bundle by design — `.next/static` is copied separately by
  `deploy/docker/web.Dockerfile`, but a stale comment in that file
  ("There is no web/public directory in this project, so none is
  copied") pre-dated slice 123's introduction of the public/ tree and
  was never updated. As a result `/logo-light.svg`, `/logo-dark.svg`,
  `/og-image.png`, `/twitter-card.png`, the PWA icons, and
  `/apple-touch-icon.png` all returned 404 in the deployed image, even
  though `proxy.ts`'s PUBLIC_STATIC_FILES set correctly let the
  requests through to the static-file handler. The fix adds a third
  `COPY` line to web.Dockerfile (`/app/web/public ./web/public`, NOT
  `./public` — the monorepo standalone tracer roots at the repo
  layout so server.js lives at `web/server.js` and public/ must be
  its sibling) and a `build:standalone` npm script in `web/package.json`
  that performs the same copy for local `node .next/standalone/web/
  server.js` invocations. Regression-guarded by a new Playwright spec
  at `web/e2e/logo-render-production-build.spec.ts` (6 assertions
  covering both logo variants + OG card + Twitter card + favicon +
  end-to-end login-page rendering) following the slice 146
  `ATLAS_PROD_BUILD` quarantine pattern.
- BFF cookie forwarding works in Next.js production-build standalone
  ([#146](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/146)). Every
  Unraid / Helm / docker-compose operator pulling main was hit by a
  regression where the dashboard / control-detail / audit-workspace /
  board-pack-preview panels rendered "Could not load this panel ·
  Unexpected token '<'... is not valid JSON" against the production-
  build standalone server (`node .next/standalone/server.js`), even
  though the same surface worked against `npm run dev`. Root cause: the
  `signIn` server action (`web/app/login/actions.ts`) set the
  `sa_session_token` cookie with `secure: process.env.NODE_ENV ===
  "production"`, which emitted the `Secure` attribute on every prod-
  build deployment — including the many self-hosted operators serving
  over plain HTTP. Browsers refuse to send Secure cookies on HTTP, so
  the BFF saw no cookie, `web/proxy.ts` redirected every `/api/**` path
  to `/login`, and the browser fetch parsed the login HTML as JSON.
  The fix replaces the blunt `NODE_ENV` check with a per-request
  transport detection (`web/lib/secure-cookie.ts::shouldUseSecureCookie`)
  that trusts the `X-Forwarded-Proto` / RFC 7239 `Forwarded` headers
  and defaults to NOT-secure when no signal is present. Unit-tested
  (8 vitest cases) and end-to-end-tested via a quarantined Playwright
  spec at `web/e2e/bff-cookie-production-build.spec.ts`. Operator-facing
  runbook at `docs/runbooks/bff-cookie-forwarding.md` explains the
  gotcha + how to test for regression.
- Control detail no longer hard-404s on fresh install
  ([#152](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/152)). On a
  fresh install the `/controls` list renders the ~1,400-row global SCF
  anchor catalog, but clicking any row navigated to
  `/controls/{anchor.id}` which the detail page passed to
  `/v1/controls/{id}/coverage` — a path that expects a tenant control
  UUID, not an SCF anchor UUID. Every click 404'd. The fix is a hybrid
  (b + c) per [ADR-0004](docs/adr/0004-control-detail-404-empty-state.md):
  the detail page now distinguishes the 404 path from 5xx and renders
  a friendly empty-state explaining honestly that "this SCF anchor has
  no control instantiated in your tenant yet" with a back-to-list CTA;
  the list page gains a truly-zero defensive empty-state for the
  catalog-not-seeded branch. The backend 404 contract is preserved
  (slice 150 D3 — bare-`{id}` 404 is a load-bearing platform semantic).
  Discriminator lives in a pure-logic helper
  (`web/app/(authed)/controls/error-classifier.ts`) with eight vitest
  cases. Auto-seeding the SOC 2 stock kit on bootstrap (option a in the
  slice doc) was rejected — full reasoning in
  `docs/audit-log/152-control-detail-404-decisions.md`. Vision §1.5 #7
  ("installable, seeded, producing first evidence within 4 hours")
  remains unmet and is the right scope for a successor slice gated on
  slice 141 multi-tenant bootstrap landing.
- Risk creation form (`/risks/new`) ships the control-link multi-select
  ([#151](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/151); slice
  105 follow-on). Slice 105 shipped `/risks/new` bound to the slice-019
  `POST /v1/risks` write path but omitted the control-link picker UI,
  so any user picking the default `mitigate` treatment hit the
  server-side validation error "treatment=mitigate requires at least
  one linked_control_id" with nowhere in the UI to satisfy it. Slice
  151 closes the loop: a new `ControlMultiSelect` component
  (`web/app/(authed)/risks/new/control-multi-select.tsx`) renders a
  search-filterable checkbox list bound to a new tenant-control list
  endpoint, and the form gates submit client-side when
  `treatment === 'mitigate'` and zero controls are selected. The
  backend gains a thin `GET /v1/controls` handler
  (`internal/api/controls/list.go`) that wraps the existing
  `ListActiveControls` sqlc query so the picker has a list endpoint to
  consume; this is distinct from the pre-existing
  `/v1/anchors?include=state` (SCF catalog) used by the `/controls`
  page. A matching BFF route lives at `/api/controls-list` (the
  pre-existing `/api/controls` route stays bound to anchors).
  Validation is extracted to a pure `validateRiskForm` fn so vitest can
  pin the client-side gate; the empty/loading/error states render
  graceful messages and the picker disappears when treatment switches
  away from `mitigate` (selection persists in form state so toggling
  back restores it). Playwright spec at
  `web/e2e/risks-create-control-link.spec.ts` is quarantined behind
  slice 082 per the established precedent (slice 094 / 098 / 100 / 105
  / 147 / 149 / 157).
- Dashboard `upcoming` and `top risks` panels now consume the slice-066
  unified rollup and `sort=residual,age` server-side ranking
  ([#157](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/157); slice
  066 follow-on; spillover from slice 147). Slice 040 wired the
  `upcoming` panel to `/v1/exceptions/expiring?within=30d` (the only
  real source on main at the time) with a labelled `upcoming-gap`
  footer naming the unified rollup as a follow-up backend gap, and
  wired `top risks` to the unsorted `treatment=mitigate` list with a
  `top-risks-sort-gap` footer naming the residual,age ranking as a
  follow-up. Slice 066 shipped both the rollup endpoint (`/v1/upcoming`
  merging exceptions, policy acks, vendor reviews, and audit-period
  milestones) and the server-side ranking (`?sort=residual,age`
  ordering by residual-score magnitude descending then risk age
  ascending); slice 147 closed the loop on two other slice-066
  follow-on panels (framework posture + activity feed); slice 157
  closes the loop on these two. The `upcoming` panel rewrites to
  consume the unified rollup row shape with a category badge per row
  (`exception` -> destructive, `audit_period` -> secondary,
  `policy_ack` and `vendor_review` -> outline) and a category-agnostic
  empty-state message. The `top risks` panel drops the
  "server order (residual/age ranking pending)" header copy and the
  gap footer. Vitest covers the two re-pointed BFF routes (4 cases
  each: 401, bearer forwarding plus the upstream URL contract, empty
  envelope, error propagation). Playwright spec at
  `web/e2e/dashboard.spec.ts` is updated for AC-3 + AC-5 with the
  new selectors, quarantined behind slice 082 per the established
  precedent.
- Audits page "Create audit period" button no longer redirects to
  `/admin` ([#149](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/149)).
  Slice 102 shipped `/audits` with the toolbar `audits-create-cta`
  disabled and the true-zero empty-state CTA placeholder-routed to
  `/admin` (slice 102 P0-A3). Operators on v1.10.0 reported clicking
  "Create audit period" bounced them to the admin overview instead of
  any period-create flow. Slice 149 ships the minimal create flow at
  `/audits/new`: a form bound directly to the slice-028 `createReq`
  wire shape (name + framework_version_id UUID + period_start +
  period_end) posting through a new `POST /api/audits` BFF handler to
  `POST /v1/audit-periods`. Both CTAs (toolbar action and empty-state
  CTA) are re-pointed to `/audits/new`. The FrameworkVersion picker is
  a UUID-paste input — copy the value from the audits-list table's
  framework-version column (the first 8 chars render with the full
  UUID in the title attribute) or from the catalog admin; a dedicated
  picker is a future enhancement once the list endpoint exists.
  Vitest covers the BFF POST (3 new cases: 401-without-cookie,
  forwards-bearer-and-body, propagates-upstream-4xx). Playwright spec
  at `web/e2e/audits-create.spec.ts` is quarantined behind slice 082
  per the established precedent.
- Empty-set robustness across `/v1/*` list endpoints — the dashboard
  panel for `GET /v1/me/acknowledgments` no longer returns 500 on a
  fresh install when the calling credential is a bootstrap-owner key
  (UserID is `key_*`, not a UUID). The handler now treats a non-UUID
  UserID as a service-account marker and returns
  `{ pending: [], count: 0, window_seconds: <int> }`. The convention
  is documented in `CONTRIBUTING.md` ("Empty-set robustness") and
  enforced by a cross-cutting integration sweep at
  `internal/api/emptyset/audit_integration_test.go` plus per-package
  empty-tenant tests for `freshnessdrift`, `policies`, `policyacks`,
  and `dashboard` ([#150](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/150)).
  Operator report on v1.10.0 surfaced three panels returning
  "Could not load this panel · 500 Internal Server Error" on a fresh
  install; the audit sweep verified the drift / policies / dashboard
  metrics endpoints were already correct (empty array + 200 envelope)
  and the only true 500-on-empty path was `/v1/me/acknowledgments`.
  Every other GET list / aggregate endpoint enumerated in the slice
  doc's suspect list (`/v1/risks`, `/v1/evidence`, `/v1/audit-periods`,
  `/v1/board-briefs`, `/v1/vendors`, `/v1/admin/users`, and 25 more)
  is now covered by the sweep as a regression gate.
- Dashboard read endpoints admitted for non-admin roles — `GET /v1/activity`
  and `GET /v1/upcoming` (slice 066) are now admitted for viewer,
  control_owner, and auditor in addition to the admin / grc_engineer
  wildcard reads they already had ([#156](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/156);
  slice 066 follow-on, paired with slice 148). Slice 066 shipped the
  three dashboard read endpoints registered at
  `internal/api/httpserver.go:603-605` but never updated the per-role
  readable-resources sets, so any non-admin / non-grc credential hitting
  the dashboard saw "Failed to load" on the Activity and Upcoming
  panels (same OPA-admit-omission shape slice 148 fixed for
  `/v1/calendar` — surfaced as spillover D8 in the slice 148 decisions
  log). `GET /v1/frameworks/posture` was already admitted via
  `defaults.rego.catalog_resources["frameworks"]` (slice 035) — the
  slice-156 matrix test pins that contract so a future narrowing of
  `catalog_resources` trips at the unit-test layer. Both
  `policies/authz/` (source of truth) and `internal/authz/rego_bundle/`
  (embedded mirror) are updated in lockstep. The OPA matrix test at
  `internal/authz/slice156_test.go` covers the 18 (endpoints × roles)
  admit cases plus 8 write-deny cases so a future maintainer
  accidentally removing one of the admits or widening to a write
  surface trips a unit-test failure.
- Compliance calendar OPA admit — `GET /v1/calendar` and
  `POST /v1/calendar/subscription` are now admitted for every
  signed-in role (admin, grc_engineer, auditor, viewer, control_owner)
  per slice 094 AC-9 intent ([#148](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/148)).
  Slice 094 shipped the calendar handler + frontend but never updated
  the OPA policies; operators on v1.10.0 with non-admin / non-grc
  credentials saw "Failed to load calendar events" because OPA
  returned `allow=false` on the new `"calendar"` resource type
  (root cause D2 in the slice 148 decisions log). Both
  `policies/authz/` (source of truth) and `internal/authz/rego_bundle/`
  (embedded mirror) are updated in lockstep; OPA matrix tests at
  `internal/authz/slice148_test.go` pin the admit set so a future
  maintainer accidentally removing one of the admits trips a unit-test
  failure. The subscription mint is path-predicated
  (`request.path == "/v1/calendar/subscription"`) rather than wildcard
  write on `"calendar"` so future write paths require an explicit
  rego edit. Spillover slice
  [#156](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/156)
  filed for the same gap on slice 066's dashboard read endpoints
  (`/v1/activity`, `/v1/upcoming`, `/v1/frameworks/posture`).

### Added

- OpenAPI 3.1 spec for the REST API + Redoc UI on the docs site +
  BLOCKING `openapi-drift-check` CI guard
  ([#140](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/140)).
  The canonical spec at `docs/openapi.yaml` is generated
  deterministically by `cmd/atlas-openapi` from the in-tree
  `internal/api/openapi.RouteSpecs` slice — single source of truth
  (slice 140 P0-A8). The BLOCKING CI guard asserts the committed
  spec is in lockstep with both the generator output AND the chi
  registrations under `internal/api/*/` (slice 140 D3 — same
  pattern as slice 128's `actions-pin-check`). The Redoc UI lives at
  `/api/` on the published mkdocs site; operator-only endpoints
  (`/health`, `/metrics`, `/v1/version`, `/v1/install-state`) carry
  `x-internal: true` and are filtered from the public render by
  `docs-site/hooks/openapi_pipeline.py` at docs build time (P0-A3
  mitigation against information disclosure). gRPC stays specified
  separately in `proto/*.proto` (P0-A7).
- Data-export library (CSV / JSON / XLSX) + audit-log export endpoint
  + Export buttons on `/audit-log` ([#135](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/135)).
  Reusable `internal/export/` package with three streaming encoders;
  reference impl at `GET /v1/admin/audit-log/export?format=...` reuses
  the slice-124 aggregator; BFF at `/api/audit-log/export` streams the
  body; Playwright + vitest + Go-integration coverage. The XLSX encoder
  is a handcrafted single-sheet-text-only writer (zero new deps,
  P0-A6 by construction). Meta-audit row written on every outcome
  (action = `audit_log_export`).

### Changed

- Hardened the slice-124 unified-audit-log SQL to defer the
  `actor_id::uuid` cast via a `CASE WHEN regex` expression, closing
  a planner-reordering footgun that surfaced during slice-135
  integration testing ([#135](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/135) D6).
- Dashboard `frameworks posture` + `recent activity` panels now render
  real data ([#147](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/147);
  slice 066 follow-on). The slice-040 `MissingEndpointPanel` placeholders
  ("This panel binds to GET /v1/frameworks/posture, which does not exist
  on main yet" / same for `/v1/activity`) reported on v1.10.0 Unraid are
  removed; both panels now consume the slice-066 backend reads via new
  BFF proxies under `/api/dashboard/framework-posture` and
  `/api/dashboard/activity`. Per-framework tiles render coverage %,
  freshness composite, and signed 90-day trend delta; the activity feed
  renders event_type / resource / actor / relative-time per row. Empty
  installs render the panels' empty-state copy, never a placeholder or
  500. The remaining two slice-066 follow-on bindings (`upcoming-panel`
  → `/v1/upcoming`; `top-risks-panel` → `?sort=residual,age`) are
  spilled to [#148](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/148).

## [1.10.0](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/compare/v1.9.0...v1.10.0) (2026-05-18)


### Features

## [Unreleased]

### Changed

- **docs:** README refreshed with v1.10.0+ baseline + updated platform-state pitch ([#132](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/132)) — refreshes the README's "v1 complete" callout to reflect operator-grade reality (120+ slices merged, v1.10.0 current release, audit-log trio 124+125+126+129+130, CI hardening trilogy 117+127+128). Adds a new "What's new in v1.10.0" section with two-bullet capability batch summaries. Drops the 1.8 MB `flow-create-control.gif` (slice 132 scope: static PNG only) and the "What it looks like in motion" subsection — the dashboard → control-detail flow is implicit from the side-by-side static screenshots. Hardens the slice-057 capture pipeline at `web/scripts/capture-readme-screenshots.ts` with the AC-2 safety gate: `assertCaptureSafe()` refuses to run unless `ATLAS_DEMO_SEED=1` is set AND the upstream HTTP target resolves to a loopback / RFC1918 private-range address. New test file `web/scripts/capture-readme-screenshots.test.ts` (26 cases — `isLoopbackOrPrivate` covers 14 branches; `assertCaptureSafe` covers 12) locks the per-branch behavior so a refactor cannot widen the admit set silently — the gate is the load-bearing information-disclosure mitigation per slice 132's threat model (every captured PNG is permanent public PII-leak vector). New `scripts/**/*.test.ts` include pattern added to `web/vitest.config.ts`. The `just refresh-screenshots` recipe drops the ffmpeg/GIF post-step, promotes pngquant from optional to required, exports `ATLAS_DEMO_SEED=1` into the script invocation, and adds a per-file + total budget gate (page ≤ 200K, hero ≤ 350K, total ≤ 2M — exit non-zero on violation). Per-image budget audit: total 288 KB / 2048 KB cap (14% utilization). All 22 relative README links + 10 image references validated. JUDGMENT-type slice — decisions log at `docs/audit-log/132-readme-refresh-decisions.md` records D1 the seed-fixture choice (slice-057 hermetic stub-server is the documented equivalent the slice doc AC-3 admits), D2 the per-image budget table, D3 the README sections changed, D4 the screenshots considered but cut (GIF + login-page + audit-log + risk-hierarchy), D5 the capture-vs-restore call (the capture pipeline ran but surfaced a non-slice-132 BFF cookie regression; restored slice-057 PNGs against the same component tree — captured 2026-05-14, no breaking dashboard / control-detail / audit-workspace / board-pack-preview UI change since), D6 the per-PNG provenance + manual-review audit (P0-A1/A2/A3 verified each), D7 the anti-criteria compliance table, D8 the test-coverage rationale (26 cases for a one-function gate because a loosened gate publishes data permanently). Anti-criteria honored (P0): no real customer data in any PNG (A1); no emails / IPs / tokens / real-org names (A2); demo-seed PII synthetic-only (A3); ≤ 2 MB total + no `git lfs` (A4); no docs/getting-started/ or docs/walkthroughs/ edits — slice 133 + 134 own those (A5); no CLAUDE.md edit — separate plain doc-PR per `/idea-to-slice` skill rule (A6); no logo asset regeneration (A7); neutral `test-*` fixture literals only (A8).

### Fixed

- **e2e:** unmask + fix 4 specs blocked by slice 119 polarity flip ([#123](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/123)) — closes the diagnose-heavy spillover from slice 119's port-3000 fix. Once Playwright actually executed specs again post-119, four specs surfaced as failing: `auth-open-redirect.spec.ts`, `first-time-login.spec.ts`, `logo-render.spec.ts`, `security-headers.spec.ts`. Per-spec diagnoses + fixes — all in production code, NONE in spec body (anti-criteria P0-A1 / P0-A2 honored; no `.skip()` / `.fixme()` / assertion relaxation):
  - **`security-headers.spec.ts`** — the slice-087 `internal/api/securityheaders/middleware.go` only covered atlas (Go) responses on port :8080, but Playwright drives the browser against Next.js on :3000. Browser-served HTML carried NONE of the five hardening headers. Fix: add an `applySecurityHeaders(res)` block to `web/proxy.ts` mirroring the slice-087 directives byte-for-byte (HSTS 1y + includeSubDomains, X-Content-Type-Options nosniff, X-Frame-Options DENY, Referrer-Policy strict-origin-when-cross-origin, CSP report-only — same hydration-violation D1 reason for report-only). Applied to every Next.js response: `/login`, `/dashboard`, BFF routes, AND public static assets + redirects (defense-in-depth so a 307-followed browser doesn't see one un-headered hop). 4 new vitest cases in `web/proxy.test.ts` lock the contract.
  - **`logo-render.spec.ts`** — the proxy matcher excluded `_next/static`, `_next/image`, and `favicon.ico` but NOT the other public assets the login page + Metadata API reference: `og-image.png`, `twitter-card.png`, `icon-192.png`, `icon-512.png`, `apple-touch-icon.png`, `logo-light.svg`, `logo-dark.svg`. Unauthenticated `page.request.get("/og-image.png")` was 307→200-text/html (the login page render), breaking `expect(...).toBe("image/png")`. Real OG scrapers would have seen the same broken unfurl. Fix: explicit `PUBLIC_STATIC_FILES` Set allow-list in `web/proxy.ts` — short + literal per the P0-A1 exact-equality discipline (a regex `\.(png|svg|ico)$` would expose any future tenant-scoped asset). 8 new vitest cases including an adjacent-path negative (`/og-image-suffix.png` still redirects).
  - **`first-time-login.spec.ts`** — the slice-073 implementation fetched `/v1/install-state` from the login page's Server Component using `apiBaseURL()`. The spec mocked via `page.route("**/v1/install-state")` — but Playwright's `page.route()` only intercepts BROWSER network traffic, NEVER server-side `fetch()` from an RSC. The mock never fired; the spec hit the real atlas response (`first_install: false` post-seed-harness), hiding the card, timing out `toBeVisible`. Fix: new BFF route at `web/app/api/install-state/route.ts` (mirrors the slice-072 `/api/version` pattern — public upstream, no bearer forwarded, 5xx → safe default per P0-A5) + extracted client island `web/components/first-install-card.tsx` that fetches the BFF from the browser. Spec mock pattern updated from `**/v1/install-state` → `**/api/install-state` (the only spec-side change — the assertion is unchanged; the mock URL was wrong about the architecture). 7 new vitest cases on the BFF route.
  - **`auth-open-redirect.spec.ts`** — self-resolved by slice 122's `api_keys_token_hash_unique` parallel-worker race fix. The auth-spec failure trace had been a downstream symptom of the seed-harness `ON CONFLICT (token_hash) DO NOTHING` gap: one of two parallel Playwright workers' `seedFromFixture()` calls would lose the race and exit non-zero, deauthenticating the spec's bearer-cookie injection before sign-in completed. With slice 122 merged, the seed is idempotent across workers and the `signIn → safeRedirectTarget → /dashboard` flow completes correctly. No production-code change needed for this spec; the slice-086 `safeRedirectTarget` defense was already correct.
  - **Per-spec last-passing audit (AC-4):** all four specs were authored under the post-slice-079 quarantine (`continue-on-error: true`) where Playwright failures were silenced; slice 119 flipped the polarity but the underlying bugs were never green in CI for these specs — they were _masked_, not _regressed_. `git log` per spec shows: `security-headers.spec.ts` (slice 087, never executed against real Next.js port :3000 until 119); `logo-render.spec.ts` (slice 075, public-asset path never exercised until 119); `first-time-login.spec.ts` (slice 073, mock-URL bug present from authoring but masked by `continue-on-error`); `auth-open-redirect.spec.ts` (slice 086, masked by the slice-082 `api_keys` race fixed in slice 122). All four were "born red" rather than regressed from a green baseline.
  - Decisions log at `docs/audit-log/123-investigate-4-unmasked-e2e-spec-failures-decisions.md` records the per-spec root-cause analysis + the production-code-vs-spec-fix scoping call + the shared-vs-independent-cause finding. No spillover slices filed: each of the four root causes was small-surface and orthogonal.

### Added

- **infra:** SHA-pin every GitHub Action across all workflows + BLOCKING `actions-pin-check` CI guard ([#128](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/128)) — closes the supply-chain gap that any non-SHA-pinned `uses:` line in any workflow exposes the project to the tag-jacking attack class. Extends slice 117's SHA-pin convention (which previously covered only `step-security/harden-runner`) to every action in every workflow: 26 unique upstream repos resolved through `gh api repos/<repo>/git/refs/tags/<tag>` (8 of them annotated-tag types that needed one extra dereference hop to the commit SHA — `actions/attest-build-provenance`, `github/codeql-action` covering 3 sub-paths, `bufbuild/buf-action`, `astral-sh/setup-uv`, `azure/setup-helm`, `aquasecurity/trivy-action`, `googleapis/release-please-action`, `sigstore/cosign-installer`). Every swept line preserves the `# <tag>` trailing comment for human readability + Dependabot's update convention. NO action version bumps (P0-A1 honored — Dependabot's job). NO workflow semantic changes — `if:` / `with:` / `env:` blocks unchanged byte-for-byte. New `scripts/check-action-pins.sh` walks all workflow files, extracts every `uses:` line (both named-step `uses: ...` and compact list-item `- uses: ...` YAML forms), asserts each ref is a 40-char lowercase-hex SHA, exits 1 with a per-line diagnostic on violation. New `scripts/check-action-pins_test.sh` covers 7 cases (pinned, tag-pinned, mixed, short-SHA, missing-dir, empty-dir, reproducibility) with 15 assertions; runs without network via the `ATLAS_WORKFLOWS_DIR` env override. New BLOCKING CI job `actions-pin-check` in `.github/workflows/ci.yml` runs the script on every PR + push to main — failure FAILS the build (unlike slices 069/089/109/120/127 which use the informational `continue-on-error: true` pattern; slice 128 is blocking because the supply-chain discipline must hold continuously). New `actions-pin-check` context added to `.github/branch-protection.json` `required_status_checks.contexts` with a `$additions_from_slice_128` annotation block recording the BLOCKING rationale; operator post-merge step is to run `bash scripts/apply-branch-protection.sh` (slice 127's apply ritual) to push the new contexts list to live GitHub branch-protection on `main`. New CONTRIBUTING.md "Action pinning" subsection documents the `uses: <action>@<sha> # <tag>` format + the `gh api` lookup procedure (with annotated-tag dereference) + the BLOCKING CI guard + the local repro. Decisions log at `docs/audit-log/128-sha-pin-all-github-actions-decisions.md` records D1 the per-action SHA resolution table (26 entries — the auditable sweep-time snapshot), D2 the Dependabot post-merge verification plan, D3 the slice-127 coordination outcome (file change + operator-apply-ritual decoupling), D4 the annotated-tag dereference edge cases. AFK-type slice; threat model HAS-MITIGATIONS — the slice IS the tag-jacking mitigation. Anti-criteria honored (P0): NO action version bumps (A1); full 40-char SHA only — no short SHAs (A2); `# <tag>` comment preserved on every line (A3); no semantic workflow changes (A5); SHAs resolved from upstream maintainer repos via `gh api` (A6); neutral test fixtures only — no vendor-prefixed tokens (A7).

- **infra:** Reconciled branch-protection drift; added drift-detect CI job + apply-ritual docs ([#127](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/127)) — closes the file ↔ live drift between `.github/branch-protection.json` (the in-tree source-of-truth from slice 050 AC-11) and the live GitHub branch-protection config on `main` that caused four PRs to sit held for hours on a phantom-blocker rationale during the 2026-05-17/18 cascade-unblock session. New `scripts/apply-branch-protection.sh` (idempotent — P0-A2 — strips `$`-prefixed annotation keys before PUT, re-reads live to verify convergence, returns exit 3 if GitHub silently drops a context the file lists). - **frontend:** Admin `/audit-log` page consuming the unified aggregation endpoint ([#125](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/125)) — new top-level route at `/audit-log` exposes the slice-124 `GET /v1/admin/audit-log/unified` endpoint as a filterable, paginated, read-only table for admins (today) and for auditors / grc_engineers once spillover slice 130 lands. Server component shell at `web/app/audit-log/page.tsx` + TanStack-Query-driven client island at `web/app/audit-log/page-client.tsx`. Filters (from, to, actor free-text, kind multi-select chips) serialize to URL query params (`?from=...&to=...&actor=...&kind=evidence,me`) so back/forward + share-links restore the same view. Cursor-paginated infinite scroll via IntersectionObserver auto-loads up to 10 pages (10,000 rows); after the ceiling the operator must click "Load more" to make further cost visible (P0-A3 / threat-model DoS posture). Row expand-for-payload via a hand-rolled details-row pattern (no new shadcn primitive dependency — D5 in the decisions log). Date pickers use native `<input type="date">` (no calendar library — D4). Each row shows `occurred_at` (local time + UTC tooltip via `<time dateTime>`), `actor_id` truncated to first 8 chars with full UUID on hover (D1 — spillover slice 129 files the backend `actor_name` extension), `kind` badge, `target_type`, `target_id`, `action`, and a toggle-expand for the raw `payload_json`. Route guard: server-component layout at `web/app/audit-log/layout.tsx` issues a `/api/admin/me` preflight server-side and `redirect()`s non-admins to `/dashboard?error=admin-only` (D7 — the slice doc says `middleware.ts`; the project's Next.js 16 file is `proxy.ts`, which gates only the cookie-presence check; role membership is checked at the layout level per the slice 060 pattern). The route-level guard is the FIRST line of defense; the slice-124 backend 403 is defense-in-depth (P0-A2). New BFF route at `web/app/api/audit-log/unified/route.ts` forwards the request to the platform backend with `Authorization: Bearer <bearer>` only — NOT extending the slice-110 `atlas_session` cookie forward surface (D8 narrow-scope rule). Typed client at `web/lib/api/audit-log.ts` exports `AUDIT_LOG_KINDS` (the canonical 9-value enum), `MAX_WINDOW_DAYS = 90` (single-source-of-truth for the backend cap), `buildUnifiedQuery`, `fetchUnifiedAuditLog`, and `AuditLogFetchError`. New vitest at `web/app/api/audit-log/unified/route.test.ts` (6 tests: 401-no-cookie, happy-path bearer + query forward + no Cookie header, 400 window invalid pass-through, 400 missing param pass-through, 403 non-admin pass-through, atlas_session cookie present but NOT forwarded slice-110 P0-A2 guard); new vitest at `web/lib/api/audit-log.test.ts` (8 tests: required params verbatim, drops empty optional fields, CSV kind join, actor trim, cursor passthrough, canonical 9-kind enum, MAX_WINDOW_DAYS == 90, AuditLogFetchError carries status). New Playwright e2e spec at `web/e2e/audit-log.spec.ts` (5 tests: admin sees rows, non-admin redirected, filter updates URL, cursor/pagination wire, P0-A1 no-edit-affordance) following the slice-079 quarantine pattern pending the broader bring-up. New seed fixture `fixtures/e2e/audit-log.sql` seeds two `feature_flag_audit_log` rows + one `evidence_audit_log` row across the demo tenant + extends `web/e2e/seed.ts` `FixtureName` to include `audit-log`. The legacy `/admin/audit` scaffold (slice 060) coexists unchanged — different path, different audience, different information layer (D10). AFK-type slice. Decisions log at `docs/audit-log/125-audit-log-page-frontend-decisions.md` records the 10 JUDGMENT calls. Two spillovers filed: slice 129 (extend slice-124 endpoint with `actor_name`) + slice 130 (extend `/api/admin/me` with role enumeration so auditors can reach the page). Anti-criteria honored (P0): read-only UI (P0-A1 — no inline edit / delete affordances anywhere); route-level role guard runs server-side BEFORE the page renders (P0-A2); UI clamps the date range at 90 days to mirror the backend cap (P0-A3); neutral `test-*` fixture tokens only (P0-A4 GitGuardian guard).
- **observability:** external audit-log sink with backpressure-to-fallback ([#126](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/126)) — closes the constitutional gap that an in-app admin can read + craft rows in the per-domain audit-log tables under slice 036's RLS policy. New `internal/audit/sink/` package exposes `Emit(ctx, unifiedlog.Entry)` (void return — D8: caller cannot mishandle a sink error) that fans out from each of the nine per-domain audit-log INSERT sites (`decision_audit_log`, `evidence_audit_log`, `exception_audit_log`, `sample_audit_log`, `audit_period_audit_log`, `aggregation_rule_audit_log`, `feature_flag_audit_log`, `me_audit_log`, `walkthrough_audit_log`) to a maintainer-configured JSONL file with per-record HMAC-SHA256 integrity tag. The canonical `unifiedlog.Entry` shape from slice 124 is re-used verbatim (D2): no struct duplication, the sink record format and the in-app aggregator format stay byte-for-byte identical forever. Fan-out is non-blocking (P0-A2 / D8): producer side does a select-with-default channel send; when the bounded channel (default 10000 records — `ATLAS_AUDIT_SINK_BUFFER_SIZE` override) overflows, the record is written to a NEW `audit_sink_failures` table (slice 036 four-policy append-only RLS pattern — `tenant_read FOR SELECT` + `tenant_write FOR INSERT WITH CHECK` under FORCE ROW LEVEL SECURITY, no UPDATE/DELETE policy, no UPDATE/DELETE grant for `atlas_app`) AND a slog ERROR is emitted (P0-A1: NEVER silent-drop). The writer goroutine batches writes (BatchFlushSize=100 records OR BatchFlushInterval=250ms quiet) with `O_APPEND|O_CREATE|O_WRONLY` for the standard concurrent-appender contract (logrotate `create` mode required — `copytruncate` breaks the open fd). New migration `20260518000000_audit_sink_failures.sql` (table + indexes + four-policy RLS + grants) is idempotent + reversible via `.down.sql`. Configuration: `ATLAS_AUDIT_SINK_PATH` (opt-in default — sink is no-op when unset, mirrors slice 121's `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT` pattern), `ATLAS_AUDIT_SINK_HMAC_KEY` (REQUIRED when path is set — D6 fail-fast: atlas refuses to boot if absent or shorter than 32 bytes, better to refuse than ship a silent integrity gap), `ATLAS_AUDIT_SINK_BUFFER_SIZE` (defaults 10000). Counters via `Sink.StatsSnapshot() (emitted, dropped, writeErrors, failureRows int64)` for ops dashboards. Test surface: 10 unit tests at `internal/audit/sink/sink_test.go` + 2 integration tests at `internal/audit/sink/integration_test.go` covering AC-7 (100 records all reach the sink within 5s with valid HMAC) and AC-8 (backpressure overflow lands in `audit_sink_failures` table — every drop produces exactly one fallback row, no panic, no silent drop). New operator docs at `docs/observability.md` document configuration + UID-separation pattern for the "external" property + logrotate gotchas + a reference Python HMAC verifier. JUDGMENT-type slice — decisions log at `docs/audit-log/126-external-audit-log-sink-decisions.md` records 10 design calls including D1 the sink-mechanism choice (picked option (a) JSONL-to-disk over the maintainer's filed lean of option (c) OTel logs via Collector; rationale: the OTel logs SDK is pre-1.0 alpha at `v0.19.0`, would add two unstable dependencies for a property that HMAC achieves transport-agnostically, JSONL composes with any operator log shipper, and the "external" property is achieved via filesystem UID ownership). Anti-criteria honored (P0): NEVER silent-drops on backpressure (A1); does NOT block the in-app INSERT on sink emit (A2); requires no new credential the deployment doesn't already have (A3); neutral `test-*` HMAC fixture only (A4); decisions log D1 documents all four mechanism options including the rejected ones (A5).
- **api:** `GET /v1/admin/audit-log/unified` — read-only UNION ALL across all nine per-domain audit-log tables ([#124](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/124)) — coexists with the slice-062 `/v1/admin/audit-log` endpoint (different wire shape, different consumer set; slice 062 reads via `admin_audit_log_v` over 8 tables, slice 124 adds `aggregation_rule_audit_log` + `walkthrough_audit_log` directly via a new `internal/audit/unifiedlog/` aggregator package). Canonical Entry shape `{occurred_at, actor_id, tenant_id, kind, target_type, target_id, action, row_id, payload_json}`; `kind` enumerates `decision | evidence | exception | sample | audit_period | aggregation_rule | feature_flag | me | walkthrough`. Tenant isolation handed off to PostgreSQL RLS via `tenancy.ApplyTenant` under `atlas_app` (slice-124 P0-A4: no BYPASSRLS); the aggregator does NOT accept a tenant_id parameter (P0-A5: implicit from session context). Defense-in-depth role gate accepts admin OR auditor OR grc_engineer (D5 in `docs/audit-log/124-unified-audit-log-aggregation-decisions.md` — the v1 GRC operator persona needs visibility into their own program). 90-day request-window cap; 1000-row cursor-paginated page; cursor opaque base64 over `{occurred_at, kind, row_id}` (the audit-row's own UUID PK guarantees per-row uniqueness across the UNION — D6 in the decisions log). Migration `20260517000000_unified_audit_log.sql` adds the only missing composite index (`(tenant_id, created_at DESC)` on `aggregation_rule_audit_log`) and extends `me_audit_log.action` CHECK to include `'audit_log_query_unified'`. Every successful query writes one `me_audit_log` row with that action value (AC-10 meta-audit). New OPA matrix tests at `internal/authz/slice124_test.go` (admin allow / auditor allow / grc_engineer allow / viewer deny / control_owner deny / no-roles deny / auditor-write deny). Integration tests at `internal/api/adminauditlog/unified_integration_test.go` cover tenant-isolation across all 9 kinds (AC-9), meta-audit row written per query (AC-10), 1500-row cursor pagination walk (AC-11), 90-day window guard (AC-5), missing-param 400 (AC-5), no-eligible-role 403. EXPLAIN ANALYZE on the UNION shows index-scan paths on 8/9 base tables (`me_audit_log` planner-chosen Seq Scan at small row counts) — documented in the decisions log (D9). AFK-type slice. Unblocks slice 125 (frontend `/audit-log` page) and slice 126 (external audit-log sink). Anti-criteria honored (P0): read-only aggregator (P0-A1, P0-A8 type-system enforced — zero exported writer); no new physical audit-log table (P0-A2 — UNION is virtual); no schema change to the nine existing audit-log tables beyond the additive me_audit_log CHECK extension (P0-A3); no BYPASSRLS (P0-A4); no tenant_id parameter at API or aggregator surface (P0-A5); OPA role check on every code path (P0-A6); neutral `test-*` fixture tokens (P0-A7).

### Changed

- **api:** Admin `/api/admin/me` includes caller role list; `/audit-log` admits auditor + grc_engineer ([#130](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/130)) — closes the slice-125 D9 follow-up. Backend slice-108 `GET /v1/me` profile shape gains a new additive `roles: []string` field sourced from `user_roles` via the shared `authz.DBRolesResolver` (same path the slice-035 OPA middleware uses — no duplicated SQL, P0-A1). The slice-060 BFF at `web/app/api/admin/me/route.ts` now proxies through `/v1/me` (instead of the admin-gated `/v1/admin/credentials` status probe — D2 in the decisions log) and forwards `{ is_admin, roles }` additively. Existing slice-060 consumers that read only `is_admin` continue to work unchanged (P0-A2 additive). Frontend slice-125 layout at `web/app/audit-log/layout.tsx` widens its server-side route guard from `is_admin === true` to `is_admin || roles.includes("auditor") || roles.includes("grc_engineer")` — the admit set matches slice-124's `HasUnifiedAuditLogRole` SQL exactly. Fail-closed posture (P0-A3): a missing or non-array `roles` field collapses to `[]` and admits only on `is_admin`. The slice-060 `/admin/*` layout is NOT widened (D5). Backend integration test surface (4 new tests at `internal/api/me/profile_integration_test.go`). 11-test vitest matrix on the BFF + 14-test predicate matrix on the layout. AFK-type slice; decisions log records 8 design calls.
- **backend:** Admin `/v1/admin/audit-log/unified` returns `actor_name` for callers with a users row ([#129](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/129)) — closes the slice 125 D1 UX gap. The aggregator query in `internal/db/queries/unified_audit_log.sql` now LEFT JOINs onto `users` (keyed on `actor_id::uuid = users.id`, with a regex pre-filter that lets non-UUID actor_ids — credential ids like `key_foo`, system literals like `seeder` — fall through cleanly without raising) and projects `users.display_name` as the additive `actor_name` field. Wire shape is JSON `null` when no users row matches (purely additive — older clients that ignore unknown fields continue to work; P0-A3). Tenant isolation: two-leg guard — RLS on `users` (load-bearing, `atlas_app` role) + explicit `ON u.tenant_id = unified.tenant_id` predicate in the JOIN clause (defense-in-depth so an accidental BYPASSRLS upgrade cannot leak cross-tenant display names through this read). Frontend (`web/lib/api/audit-log.ts` + `web/app/audit-log/page-client.tsx`): the actor column now renders the resolved display name with the full `actor_id` exposed via tooltip; falls back to the slice-125 truncated-UUID render when `actor_name` is null OR undefined (P0-A6 graceful-degrade against older backends). New renderer helper `renderActorLabel` + `truncateActorId` extracted into `web/lib/api/audit-log.ts` so the contract can be vitest-locked without a JSX render harness. Tests: 3 new Go integration tests at `internal/api/adminauditlog/unified_integration_test.go` (AC-3 happy resolve, AC-4 null-on-wire + literal `"actor_name":null` body check, P0-A1 cross-tenant RLS isolation via a `leaked-secret` user seeded in Tenant B then audit-rowed in Tenant A); 9 new vitest cases at `web/lib/api/audit-log.test.ts`. sqlc regen on this slice: re-applied the three slice 109 hand-narrows. JUDGMENT-type slice; decisions log records 7 design calls.
- **frontend:** BFF forwards `atlas_session` cookie on `/api/me/sessions*` ([#110](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/110)) — closes the slice 108 D4 UX gap. The three `/api/me/sessions*` BFF routes (`GET /api/me/sessions`, `DELETE /api/me/sessions`, `DELETE /api/me/sessions/{id}`) now forward the slice-034 `atlas_session` cookie alongside the existing `sa_session_token` bearer, so the slice-108 backend can flag the caller's current session row (`is_current: true`) and so the slice-103 `/settings` Active Sessions section can render a "current" badge. New `OIDC_SESSION_COOKIE = "atlas_session"` constant exported from `web/lib/auth.ts` with a doc comment pinning the narrow scope. New shared helper `web/app/api/me/sessions/_headers.ts::buildSessionsForwardHeaders(bearer, oidc)` colocated INSIDE the sessions directory on purpose (P0-A2: cookie scope is narrow — other BFF routes MUST NOT import it). Helper validates the cookie value against the slice-034 URL-safe-base64 alphabet (`/^[A-Za-z0-9_-]+$/`) and silently drops anything that fails, preventing a header-injection vector via a malformed cookie value (graceful degrade: platform sees no cookie → returns unflagged rows honestly). NO change to bearer-auth semantic — `sa_session_token` remains the primary auth carrier (P0-A2). NO change to `/api/me` profile or `/api/me/preferences` routes (P0-A1). NO backend change — slice 108 already reads `r.Cookie("atlas_session")`. New vitest coverage: 7 tests at `web/app/api/me/sessions/route.test.ts` (GET 401-no-bearer + GET forwards-both + GET omits-Cookie-when-absent + GET drops-malformed-injection + DELETE 401-no-bearer + DELETE forwards-both + DELETE omits-Cookie-when-absent); 3 tests at `web/app/api/me/sessions/[id]/route.test.ts` (DELETE 401-no-bearer + DELETE forwards-both-and-path + DELETE omits-Cookie-when-absent). Neutral `test-*` fixture tokens only (P0-A4 GitGuardian guard). AFK-type slice.

### Added

- **infra:** atlas OTel SDK integration (traces + metrics + Go runtime telemetry across HTTP/DB/NATS surfaces) ([#121](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/121)) — wires the atlas-side OpenTelemetry SDK end-to-end so the receive-side backplane shipped by PR #234 (OTel Collector + Tempo + Prometheus at `deploy/observability/`) finally has a producer. New `internal/observability/otel/` package: `Init(ctx, opts)` configures `TracerProvider` + `MeterProvider` + the W3C TraceContext + Baggage propagators with OTel-standard env-var configuration (`OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT`, `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_PROTOCOL`, `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME`, `OTEL_RESOURCE_ATTRIBUTES`, `OTEL_TRACES_SAMPLER`, `OTEL_TRACES_SAMPLER_ARG`); no custom `ATLAS_OTEL_*` namespace (P0-A2). NO-OP when `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT` is unset (AC-2 / P0-A12): atlas serves traffic with zero telemetry overhead, the property that keeps the single-binary self-host story honest. HTTP server: `otelhttp.NewHandler(root, "atlas-http")` at the outermost middleware layer so every request including 401s gets a span; default attribute shape (`http.method`, `http.route`, `http.status_code`, `http.target`, `net.peer.ip`) — NO Authorization / Cookie / body recording (P0-A7 / P0-A8). High-frequency probes (`/health`, `/metrics`, `/v1/version`, `/v1/install-state`) excluded from span generation via `otelhttp.WithFilter` (AC-7). DB pool: all eight `pgxpool.New` call sites in `cmd/atlas/main.go` routed through `atlasotel.NewTracedPool`, which attaches the `otelpgx` tracer; `db.statement` keeps `$N` placeholders, parameter literal values are NEVER attribute-recorded (P0-A9). NATS: producer-side span on each `JetStreamPublisher.Publish` with W3C `traceparent` header injection; consumer extracts the header and starts a linked child span, so evidence-ingest is one trace from HTTP push → publisher span → consumer span → DB write. Message body NEVER on a span attribute — only subject + idempotency key (P0-A8 + AC-13). Go runtime metrics auto-emitted at 15s cadence via `go.opentelemetry.io/contrib/instrumentation/runtime` (`runtime.go.goroutines`, `runtime.go.gc.pause_total_ns`, `runtime.go.mem.heap_alloc`, `runtime.go.mem.heap_inuse`, `runtime.go.mem.lookups`, `runtime.go.cgo.calls`, `runtime.uptime`). Opt-in Prometheus `/metrics` fallback via `ATLAS_METRICS_FALLBACK_ENABLE=true` (DEFAULT OFF — P0-A3); when on, the route is bearer- and authz-exempt (same pattern as `/v1/version` from slice 092 — exact-path match) and operators MUST gate it at the network layer. Sampling defaults to `parentbased_traceidratio` at 10% (P0-A5); operators can crank for debugging via env-vars. Bounded async batch span processor only (P0-A4) — a slow OTel Collector can never block the request path. `cmd/atlas/main.go` startup line `atlas: opentelemetry: enabled endpoint=... sampler=... ...` (or `disabled` when off) so operators grepping logs can confirm state in one query (AC-4). New Go unit tests at `internal/observability/otel/otel_test.go` (5 tests: no-op-when-unset + service-name resolution × 2 + parseFloat + propagator composition); new integration tests at `internal/observability/otel/integration_test.go` (5 tests using `tracetest.InMemoryExporter`: bearer-token absent from any span attribute via the `test-bearer-sentinel-do-not-leak-12345` guard, NATS publisher → consumer trace-context linkage with parent-span-ID equality, NATS body absent from span attributes via `secret-payload-test-do-not-leak-abcdef` guard, publish-error stamps span Error status, consumer span uses SpanKindConsumer). New unit tests at `internal/api/metrics_endpoint_test.go` (4 tests: 404 when fallback disabled, 200 + Prometheus exposition when enabled, exemption scope is exact-path not prefix, span filter excludes the four high-frequency probes but keeps app paths). Docs: `deploy/docker/.env.example` adds the `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT` + `ATLAS_DEPLOYMENT_ENVIRONMENT` + `ATLAS_METRICS_FALLBACK_ENABLE` blocks with the network-layer-gating warning; `deploy/docker/docker-compose.yml` forwards every relevant OTEL_* env-var through the atlas service environment (no-op when unset); `deploy/observability/README.md` flips the Metrics / Traces status from "backplane ready" to "Working", documents the post-deploy smoke procedure (startup-log grep + curl traffic + Tempo / Prometheus / Grafana trace-to-logs verification). JUDGMENT-type slice — decisions log at `docs/audit-log/121-atlas-otel-sdk-decisions.md` records the 7 design calls (OTel SDK v1.34.0 + otelpgx v0.10.0 baseline; service.name=security-atlas resource attribute vs "atlas-http" otelhttp operation name; gRPC default OTLP protocol; hand-rolled NATS propagation over `nats.Header` since OTel ships no first-party NATS contrib; outermost otelhttp wrap; opt-in /metrics; deterministic sampler default). All AC pass surfaces green (`go test ./...` + `go test -tags=integration ./internal/observability/...`).

- **api:** `GET /v1/policies?include=ack_rate` join + `/policies` real ack-rate cells ([#107](https://github.com/mgoodric/security-atlas/issues/107)) — additive `?include=ack_rate` query parameter on `GET /v1/policies` returns the policy list LEFT JOINed to the per-policy acknowledgment-rate cell. Implemented as a **single SQL query** with two correlated scalar subqueries (denominator + numerator) — explicitly NOT a per-policy loop calling `AckStore.Rate` (the slice exists to avoid the 50-call fan-out anti-pattern slice 101 P0-A2 forbids). Predicates mirror `CountRequiredRoleUsersForVersion` (denominator) + `CountFreshAcksForVersion` (numerator) verbatim — same role-intersect EXISTS clause, same freshness cutoff parameter, same `api_keys` slice-034 stand-in. Wire shape: `{policies: [{...policyWire, ack_rate: cell | null}], count}` — additive; callers that omit `?include=ack_rate` continue to receive the v1 policy-only shape unchanged. Non-published policies (draft / under_review / approved / superseded) return `ack_rate: null` because the SQL CASE WHEN status='published' branch did not fire — the wire layer renders the em-dash branch honestly. Published policies with zero denominator (no required-role users) return a populated cell with `percent: null` (matches the slice-023 `rateResponse` semantic — consumers distinguish "0% acknowledged" from "no required-role members exist"). Backend constitutional invariants honored: #6 (RLS — the join runs in a `tenancy.ApplyTenant` transaction, integration test asserts Tenant A's request never sees Tenant B's ack rows); #9 (manual evidence first-class — the join is uniform whether the policy was manually authored or imported from a vendor template). Frontend: `web/lib/api.ts` hard-codes `?include=ack_rate` on both `listPolicies` (BFF) and `fetchPoliciesList` (browser) — mirrors slice 104's hard-coded `?include=state` for anchors; `web/app/(authed)/policies/page.tsx` removes the "awaiting publish or ack-rate join" placeholder copy and renders real `<Progress>` cells when the joined cell is populated. New Go unit tests at `internal/api/policies/ack_rate_unit_test.go` (6 cases: published with acks, non-published null-branch across 4 statuses, zero-denominator percent-null, parser across plain/CSV/repeated/whitespace, embedded `policyWire` shape preservation, orphan_policy warning); new Go integration tests at `internal/api/policies/ack_rate_integration_test.go` (5 cases: omitted-include shape unchanged, draft-only all-null branch, published-with-ack populated cell, RLS round-trip Tenant A vs Tenant B, cross-check that joined math equals per-policy `/v1/policies/{id}/acknowledgment-rate` output). New vitest case in `web/app/api/policies/route.test.ts` pinning the `?include=ack_rate` query-string forward. Spillover from slice 101.
